    55	
    56	import static java.lang.System.Logger.Level.DEBUG;
    57	import static java.lang.System.Logger.Level.TRACE;
    58	import static java.lang.System.Logger.Level.WARNING;
    59	
    60	/**
    61	 * Representation of a single channel between client and server.
    62	 * Everything in this class runs in the channel reader virtual thread
    63	 */
    64	class ConnectionHandler implements InterruptableTask<Void>, ConnectionContext {
    65	    private static final System.Logger LOGGER = System.getLogger(ConnectionHandler.class.getName());
    66	    private static final String HTTP_1_0 = "HTTP/1.0\r";
    67	
    68	    private final ListenerContext listenerContext;
    69	    // we must safely release the semaphore whenever this connection is finished, so other connections can be created!
    70	    private final Semaphore connectionSemaphore;
    71	    private final Limit requestLimit;
    72	    private final ConnectionProviders connectionProviders;
    73	    private final List<ServerConnectionSelector> providerCandidates;
    74	    private final Map<String, ServerConnection> activeConnections;
    75	    private final SocketChannel socket;
    76	    private final String serverChannelId;
    77	    private final Router router;
    78	    private final Tls tls;
    79	    private final ListenerConfig listenerConfig;
    80	
    81	    private ServerConnection connection;
    82	    private HelidonSocket helidonSocket;
    83	    private DataReader reader;
    84	    private SocketWriter writer;
    85	    private ProxyProtocolData proxyProtocolData;
    86	
    87	    ConnectionHandler(ListenerContext listenerContext,
    88	                      Semaphore connectionSemaphore,
    89	                      Limit requestLimit,
    90	                      ConnectionProviders connectionProviders,
    91	                      Map<String, ServerConnection> activeConnections,
    92	                      SocketChannel socket,
    93	                      String serverChannelId,
    94	                      Router router,
    95	                      Tls tls) {
    96	        this.listenerContext = listenerContext;
    97	        this.connectionSemaphore = connectionSemaphore;
    98	        this.requestLimit = requestLimit;
    99	        this.connectionProviders = connectionProviders;
   100	        this.providerCandidates = connectionProviders.providerCandidates();
   101	        this.activeConnections = activeConnections;
   102	        this.socket = socket;
   103	        this.serverChannelId = serverChannelId;
   104	        this.router = router;
   105	        this.tls = tls;
   106	        this.listenerConfig = listenerContext.config();
   107	    }
   108	
   109	    @Override
   110	    public boolean canInterrupt() {
   111	        return connection instanceof InterruptableTask<?> task && task.canInterrupt();
   112	    }
   113	
   114	    @Override
   115	    public final void run() {
   116	        String channelId = "0x" + HexFormat.of().toHexDigits(System.identityHashCode(socket));
   117	
   118	        // proxy protocol before SSL handshake
   119	        if (listenerConfig.enableProxyProtocol()) {
   120	            ProxyProtocolHandler handler = new ProxyProtocolHandler(socket, channelId);
   121	            try {
   122	                proxyProtocolData = handler.get();
   123	            } catch (RuntimeException e) {
   124	                if (LOGGER.isLoggable(TRACE)) {
   125	                    LOGGER.log(TRACE, "[" + channelId + "] Failed to retrieve Proxy Protocol data", e);
   126	                }
   127	                closeChannel(channelId);
   128	                return;
   129	            }
   130	        }
   131	
   132	        // handle SSL and init helidonSocket, reader and writer
   133	        try {
   134	            helidonSocket = createSocket(tls, socket, channelId);
   135	
   136	            reader = DataReader.create(new MapExceptionDataSupplier(helidonSocket));
   137	            writer = SocketWriter.create(listenerContext.executor(),
   138	                                         helidonSocket,
   139	                                         listenerConfig.writeQueueLength(),
   140	                                         listenerConfig.smartAsyncWrites());
   141	        } catch (RuntimeException e) {
   142	            // these exceptions are thrown to the executor service
   143	            if (LOGGER.isLoggable(TRACE)) {
   144	                LOGGER.log(TRACE, "[" + channelId + "] Failed to establish connection", e);
   145	            }
   146	            closeChannel(channelId);
   147	            return;
   148	        } catch (Exception e) {
   149	            if (LOGGER.isLoggable(TRACE)) {
   150	                LOGGER.log(TRACE, "[" + channelId + "] Failed to establish connection", e);
   151	            }
   152	            closeChannel(channelId);
   153	            return;
   154	        }
   155	
   156	        // connection handling
   157	        String socketsId = helidonSocket.socketId() + " " + helidonSocket.childSocketId();
   158	        Thread.currentThread().setName("[" + socketsId + "] WebServer socket");
   159	        if (LOGGER.isLoggable(DEBUG)) {
   160	            helidonSocket.log(LOGGER,
   161	                       DEBUG,
   162	                       "accepted socket from %s:%d",
   163	                       helidonSocket.remotePeer().host(),
   164	                       helidonSocket.remotePeer().port());
   165	        }
   166	
   167	        try {
   168	            if (helidonSocket.protocolNegotiated()) {
   169	                this.connection = connectionProviders.byApplicationProtocol(helidonSocket.protocol())
   170	                        .connection(this);
   171	            }
   172	
   173	            if (connection == null) {
   174	                this.connection = identifyConnection();
   175	            }
   176	
   177	            if (connection == null) {
   178	                if (isHttp10Connection(reader)) {
   179	                    // cannot easily return 505, so log better message instead
   180	                    throw new CloseConnectionException("HTTP 1.0 is not supported, consider using HTTP 1.1");
   181	                }
   182	                throw new CloseConnectionException("No suitable connection provider");
   183	            }
   184	            activeConnections.put(socketsId, connection);
   185	            connection.handle(requestLimit);
   186	        } catch (RequestException e) {
   187	            helidonSocket.log(LOGGER, WARNING, "escaped Request exception", e);
   188	        } catch (HttpException e) {
   189	            helidonSocket.log(LOGGER, WARNING, "escaped HTTP exception", e);
   190	        } catch (ServerConnectionException e) {
   191	            // socket exception - the socket failed, probably killed by OS, proxy or client
   192	            helidonSocket.log(LOGGER, TRACE, "server I/O issue", e);
   193	        } catch (CloseConnectionException e) {
   194	            // end of request stream - safe to close the connection, as it was requested by our client
   195	            helidonSocket.log(LOGGER, TRACE, "connection close requested", e);
   196	        } catch (UncheckedIOException e) {
   197	            if (e.getCause() instanceof SocketException) {
   198	                // socket exception - the socket failed, probably killed by OS, proxy or client
   199	                helidonSocket.log(LOGGER, TRACE, "server I/O issue", e);
   200	            } else {
   201	                helidonSocket.log(LOGGER, WARNING, "unexpected I/O exception", e);
   202	            }
   203	        } catch (Exception e) {
   204	            helidonSocket.log(LOGGER, WARNING, "unexpected exception", e);
   205	        } finally {
   206	            // connection has finished the loop of handling, release the semaphore
   207	            connectionSemaphore.release();
   208	            activeConnections.remove(socketsId);
   209	            writer.close();
   210	            closeChannel(channelId);
   211	        }
   212	
   213	        helidonSocket.log(LOGGER, DEBUG, "socket closed");
   214	    }
   215

   276	    private HelidonSocket createSocket(Tls tls, SocketChannel socket, String channelId) throws IOException {
   277	        if (listenerConfig.useNio()) {
   278	          return createNioSocket(tls, socket, channelId);
   279	        }
   280	        return createByteSocket(tls, socket, channelId);
   281	    }
   282	
   283	    private HelidonSocket createNioSocket(Tls tls, SocketChannel channel, String channelId) {
   284	        if (tls.enabled()) {
   285	            var address = channel.socket().getRemoteSocketAddress();
   286	
   287	            SSLEngine engine;
   288	            if (address instanceof InetSocketAddress isa) {
   289	                engine = tls.sslContext().createSSLEngine(isa.getHostName(), isa.getPort());
   290	            } else {
   291	                engine = tls.sslContext().createSSLEngine();
   292	            }
   293	
   294	            SSLParameters parameters = tls.sslParameters();
   295	            parameters.setEndpointIdentificationAlgorithm("");
   296	            engine.setSSLParameters(parameters);
   297	
   298	            engine.setHandshakeApplicationProtocolSelector((sslEngine, list) -> {
   299	                for (String protocolId : list) {
   300	                    if (connectionProviders.supportedApplicationProtocols()
   301	                            .contains(protocolId)) {
   302	                        return protocolId;
   303	                    }
   304	                }
   305	                return null;
   306	            });
   307	
   308	            return TlsNioSocket
   309	                    .server(channel, engine, channelId, serverChannelId);
   310	        }
   311	        return NioSocket.server(channel, channelId, serverChannelId);
   312	    }
   313	
   314	    private HelidonSocket createByteSocket(Tls tls, SocketChannel channel, String channelId) throws IOException {
   315	        if (tls.enabled()) {
   316	            SSLSocket sslSocket = (SSLSocket) tls.sslContext()
   317	                    .getSocketFactory()
   318	                    .createSocket(channel.socket(), null, false);
   319	            sslSocket.setHandshakeApplicationProtocolSelector(
   320	                    (sslEngine, list) -> {
   321	                        for (String protocolId : list) {
   322	                            if (connectionProviders.supportedApplicationProtocols()
   323	                                    .contains(protocolId)) {
   324	                                return protocolId;
   325	                            }
   326	                        }
   327	                        return null;
   328	                    });
   329	            sslSocket.startHandshake();
   330	            return TlsSocket.server(sslSocket, channelId, serverChannelId);
   331	        }
   332	        return PlainSocket.server(channel.socket(), channelId, serverChannelId);
   333	    }
   334	
   335	    private ServerConnection identifyConnection() {
   336	        // if just one candidate, take a chance with it
   337	        if (providerCandidates.size() == 1) {
   338	            return providerCandidates.getFirst().connection(this);
   339	        }
   340	
   341	        try {
   342	            reader.ensureAvailable();
   343	        } catch (DataReader.InsufficientDataAvailableException e) {
   344	            throw new CloseConnectionException("No data available", e);
   345	        }
   346	
   347	        // never move position of the reader
   348	        BufferData currentBuffer = reader.getBuffer(reader.available());
   349	
   350	        // go through candidates until we identify what kind of connection we have (now this will be either HTTP/1 or HTTP/2)
   351	        while (true) {
   352	            Iterator<ServerConnectionSelector> iterator = providerCandidates.iterator();
   353	            if (!iterator.hasNext()) {
   354	                helidonSocket.log(LOGGER, DEBUG, "Could not find a suitable connection provider. "
   355	                                + "initial connection buffer (may be empty if no providers exist):\n%s",
   356	                        currentBuffer.debugDataHex(false));
   357	                return null;
   358	            }
   359	
   360	            // check if we can identify which connection to use based on the available data
   361	            while (iterator.hasNext()) {
   362	                ServerConnectionSelector candidate = iterator.next();
   363	                int expectedBytes = candidate.bytesToIdentifyConnection();
   364	
   365	                ServerConnectionSelector.Support supports;
   366	                if (expectedBytes == 0 || expectedBytes < currentBuffer.available()) {
   367	                    supports = candidate.supports(currentBuffer);
   368	                } else {
   369	                    // we need more data, let's keep this provider for now
   370	                    continue;
   371	                }
   372	
   373	                switch (supports) {
   374	                case SUPPORTED -> {
   375	                    return candidate.connection(this);
   376	                }
   377	                // we are no longer interested in this connection provider, remove it from our list
   378	                case UNSUPPORTED -> iterator.remove();
   379	                case UNKNOWN -> {
   380	                    // we may still use it if it accepts any # of bytes, otherwise remove it (and this is a
   381	                    // wrong response...)
   382	                    if (expectedBytes != 0) {
   383	                        iterator.remove();
   384	                    }
   385	                }
   386	                default -> throw new IllegalStateException("Unknown support (" + supports
   387	                                                                   + ") returned from provider "
   388	                                                                   + candidate.getClass().getName());
   389	                }
   390	                currentBuffer.rewind();
   391	            }
   392	
   393	            // we may have removed all candidates, we must re-check
   394	            // we must return before requesting more data (as more data may not be available)
   395	            if (providerCandidates.isEmpty()) {
   396	                helidonSocket.log(LOGGER,
   397	                        DEBUG,
   398	                        "Could not find a suitable connection provider. "
   399	                                + "initial connection buffer (may be empty if no providers exist):\n%s",
   400	                        currentBuffer.debugDataHex(true));
   401	
   402	                return null;
   403	            }
   404	
   405	            // read next data (need to create a copy, to make sure we do not re-use the same buffer)
   406	            currentBuffer = reader.getBuffer(reader.available() + 1); // for additional read
   407	        }
   408	    }
   409	
   410	    private void closeChannel(String channelId) {
   411	        if (helidonSocket == null) {
   412	            try {
   413	                socket.close();
   414	            } catch (Throwable e) {
   415	                if (LOGGER.isLoggable(TRACE)) {
   416	                    LOGGER.log(TRACE, "[" + channelId + "] Failed to establish connection", e);
   417	                }
   418	            }
   419	        } else {
   420	            try {
   421	                helidonSocket.close();
   422	            } catch (Throwable e) {
   423	                helidonSocket.log(LOGGER, TRACE, "Failed to close socket on connection close", e);
   424	            }
   425	        }
   426	    }
   427	
   428	    static boolean isHttp10Connection(DataReader reader) {
   429	        try {
   430	            reader.ensureAvailable();
   431	        } catch (DataReader.InsufficientDataAvailableException e) {
   432	            throw new CloseConnectionException("No data available", e);
   433	        }
   434	        BufferData request = reader.getBuffer(reader.available());
   435	        int lf = request.indexOf(Bytes.LF_BYTE);
   436	        return lf != -1 && request.readString(lf).endsWith(HTTP_1_0);
   437	    }
   438	
   439	    private static class MapExceptionDataSupplier implements Supplier<byte[]> {
   440	        private final HelidonSocket helidonSocket;
   441	
   442	        private MapExceptionDataSupplier(HelidonSocket helidonSocket) {
   443	            this.helidonSocket = helidonSocket;
   444	        }
   445	
   446	        @Override
   447	        public byte[] get() {
   448	            try {
   449	                return helidonSocket.get();
   450	            } catch (UncheckedIOException e) {
   451	                throw new ServerConnectionException("Failed to get data from socket", e);
   452	            }
   453	        }
   454	    }
   455	}

The issue is about intermittent failures with chunked transfer encoding. Let me look at `writeChunked` again:\n\n```java\nprivate void writeChunked(BufferData buffer) {\n    int available = buffer.available();\n    byte[] hex = Integer.toHexString(available).getBytes(StandardCharsets.US_ASCII);\n\n    BufferData toWrite = BufferData.create(available + hex.length + 4);\n    toWrite.write(hex);\n    toWrite.write(\'\\r\');\n    toWrite.write(\'\\n\');\n    toWrite.write(buffer);\n    toWrite.write(\'\\r\');\n    toWrite.write(\'\\n\');\n\n    sendListener.data(ctx, toWrite);\n    responseBytesTotal += toWrite.available();\n    dataWriter.write(toWrite);\n}\n```\n\nThe problem could be in the `write` method of `FixedBufferData`:\n\n```java\npublic void write(BufferData toWrite) {\n    byte[] buffer = new byte[length - writePosition];\n    int read = toWrite.read(buffer);\n    System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);\n    writePosition += read;\n}\n```\n\nWait! This has `length - writePosition` which should be exactly `available + hex.length + 4` since we just created the buffer with that capacity. But actually, when we call `toWrite.write(hex)`, it writes `hex.length` bytes and advances `writePosition`. Then we write `\\r`, `\\n`, then the buffer, then `\\r`, `\\n`. So all should fit exactly.\n\nBut wait, let me look at the `FixedBufferData.write(BufferData toWrite)` method again more carefully:\n\n```java\npublic void write(BufferData toWrite) {\n    byte[] buffer = new byte[length - writePosition];\n    int read = toWrite.read(buffer);\n    System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);\n    writePosition += read;\n}\n```\n\nThe issue is that `toWrite.read(buffer)` returns `Math.min(buffer.length, toWrite.available())`. If `toWrite` has more bytes than the remaining space in `this.bytes`, only `buffer.length` bytes will be copied. But `buffer.length` should be exactly the right size since the buffer was allocated with the correct size.\n\nHmm, but what if the buffer is a `ReadOnlyArrayData` or `CompositeBufferData`? Let me trace through:\n\n1. In `writeChunked`, `buffer` is a `BufferData` from the application. \n2. `buffer.available()` returns the number of unread bytes.\n3. This should be fine.\n\nBut let me look at the `FixedBufferData.write(BufferData toWrite, int length)` method:\n```java\npublic void write(BufferData toWrite, int length) {\n    byte[] buffer = new byte[length];\n    int read = toWrite.read(buffer);\n    System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);\n    writePosition += read;\n}\n```\n\nThis is different! Maybe the issue is not in the chunked encoding itself but in the async writer or the socket write. Let me look at the `SmartSocketWriter` more carefully.\n\nLooking at `SmartSocketWriter`:\n\n```java\npublic void write(BufferData buffer) {\n    if (asyncMode) {\n        asyncWriter.write(buffer);\n        if (++windowIndex % WINDOW_SIZE == 0 && asyncWriter.avgQueueSize() < QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD) {\n            asyncMode = false;\n        }\n    } else {\n        asyncWriter.drainQueue();\n        writeNow(buffer);       // blocking write\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWhen `asyncMode` switches to `false`, it calls `asyncWriter.drainQueue()` and then `writeNow(buffer)`. But there\'s a race condition! The `asyncWriter` has its own thread that\'s consuming from the queue. When `asyncMode` becomes false, the `asyncWriter`\'s thread might still be running and processing buffers. So `drainQueue()` might not drain all buffers (some might have been consumed by the thread already). Meanwhile, the main thread calls `drainQueue()` and then `writeNow(buffer)`. But `CompositeListBufferData` (which is the implementation of `BufferData.createComposite(first)`) doesn\'t override `writeTo` for the composite case - it falls through to `CompositeListBufferData.writeTo`.\n\nLet me look at this more carefully. Actually, I think the real problem might be in the `CompositeListBufferData.writeTo` method or in how the composite buffer is written via NIO.\n\nLet me look at `CompositeListBufferData.writeTo`:\n\n```java\npublic int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int limit) {\n    int written = 0;\n    for (BufferData datum : data) {\n        if (datum.consumed()) {\n            continue;\n        }\n        int datumWrote = datum.writeTo(writeBuffer, limit - written);\n        if (datumWrote == 0) {\n            // not consumed and wrote 0 -> full\n            break;\n        }\n        written += datumWrote;\n    }\n    return written;\n}\n```\n\nAnd `NioSocket.write`:\n```java\npublic void write(BufferData buffer) {\n    try {\n        while (!buffer.consumed()) {\n            writeBuffer.clear();\n            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());\n            writeBuffer.flip();\n            delegate.write(writeBuffer);\n        }\n    } catch (IOException e) {\n        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWait! But `buffer.available()` may decrease as we write (since `writeTo` advances read positions). The issue might be a race condition in the switch from async to sync mode.\n\nActually, let me look at `SocketWriterAsync` again. There\'s a `close()` method:\n\n```java\npublic void close() {\n    run = false;\n    if (!started.get()) {\n        // thread never started\n        return;\n    }\n    try {\n        writeQueue.put(CLOSING_TOKEN); // wake up blocked take() operation\n        if (cdl.await(1000, TimeUnit.MILLISECONDS)) {\n            // reads finished because we set run to false\n            BufferData available;\n            while ((available = writeQueue.poll()) != null) {\n                try {\n                    writeNow(available);\n                } catch (Exception e) {\n                    LOGGER.log(System.Logger.Level.TRACE, "Failed to write last buffers during writer shutdown", e);\n                }\n            }\n        }\n        if (thread != null) {\n            thread.interrupt();\n        }\n    } catch (InterruptedException e) {\n    }\n}\n```\n\nBut this is only called on connection close. \n\nNow let me look at the problem from a different angle. The PR description says:\n- "If using chunked transfer, I occasionally see \'missing CR\' or \'Malformed encoding found in chunked-encoding\'"\n- "If sending content-length header, the transfer occasionally just gets stuck completely"\n\nThe "gets stuck completely" with content-length is interesting. Let me look at the `write` method in `BlockingOutputStream` for non-chunked (content-length) case:\n\n```java\nif (!isChunked) {\n    if (firstByte) {\n        firstByte = false;\n        Status usedStatus = status.get();\n        sendListener.status(ctx, usedStatus);\n        sendListener.headers(ctx, headers);\n        // write headers and payload part in one buffer to avoid TCP/ACK delay problems\n        BufferData growing = BufferData.growing(256 + buffer.available());\n        nonEntityBytes(headers, usedStatus, growing, keepAlive, validateHeaders);\n        // check not exceeding content-length\n        bytesWritten += buffer.available();\n        checkContentLength(buffer);\n        sendListener.data(ctx, buffer);\n        // write single buffer headers and payload part\n        growing.write(buffer);\n        responseBytesTotal += growing.available();\n        dataWriter.write(growing);\n    } else {\n        // if not chunked, always write\n        writeContent(buffer);\n    }\n    return;\n}\n```\n\nFor the first byte with content-length, it creates a growing buffer, writes headers + payload, then sends it with `dataWriter.write(growing)`. \n\nFor subsequent writes: `writeContent(buffer)` calls `dataWriter.write(buffer)`.\n\nNow, the issue with "gets stuck completely" could happen if the `SmartSocketWriter` or `SocketWriterAsync` has a threading issue. Let me think about this...\n\nActually, looking at the `SmartSocketWriter` more carefully:\n\n1. `asyncMode` starts as `true`\n2. Each write goes to `asyncWriter.write(buffer)` which puts it in a queue\n3. Every `WINDOW_SIZE` (1000) writes, it checks `avgQueueSize < 2.0`\n4. If yes, it switches to sync mode: `asyncMode = false`\n5. In sync mode: `asyncWriter.drainQueue()` then `writeNow(buffer)`\n\nThe issue: `avgQueueSize` is computed in the async thread as `(avgQueueSize + queueSize) / 2.0`. But the async thread might be delayed, so `avgQueueSize` might not reflect the current state. More importantly, `windowIndex` is incremented in the calling thread (the HTTP handler thread), while `avgQueueSize` is updated in the async writer thread.\n\nBut the real problem I think is about concurrent access. When `asyncMode = false` is set, the calling thread drains the queue and writes directly. But the async thread might still be running and processing its current batch. This could lead to:\n1. The async thread writes its composite buffer (from `writeNow(toWrite)`)\n2. The main thread drains the queue (grabbing remaining buffers)\n3. The main thread writes those drained buffers\n4. Now let me focus on the actual problem. The issue is about intermittent failures with chunked transfer encoding. Let me look at `writeChunked` again:

```java
private void writeChunked(BufferData buffer) {
    int available = buffer.available();
    byte[] hex = Integer.toHexString(available).getBytes(StandardCharsets.US_ASCII);

    BufferData toWrite = BufferData.create(available + hex.length + 4);
    toWrite.write(hex);
    toWrite.write('\r');
    toWrite.write('\n');
    toWrite.write(buffer);
    toWrite.write('\r');
    toWrite.write('\n');

    sendListener.data(ctx, toWrite);
    responseBytesTotal += toWrite.available();
    dataWriter.write(toWrite);
}
```

The problem could be in the `write` method of `FixedBufferData`:

```java
public void write(BufferData toWrite) {
    byte[] buffer = new byte[length - writePosition];
    int read = toWrite.read(buffer);
    System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);
    writePosition += read;
}
```

Wait! This has `length - writePosition` which should be exactly `available + hex.length + 4` since we just created the buffer with that capacity. But actually, when we call `toWrite.write(hex)`, it writes `hex.length` bytes and advances `writePosition`. Then we write `\r`, `\n`, then the buffer, then `\r`, `\n`. So all should fit exactly.

But wait, let me look at the `FixedBufferData.write(BufferData toWrite)` method again more carefully:

```java
public void write(BufferData toWrite) {
    byte[] buffer = new byte[length - writePosition];
    int read = toWrite.read(buffer);
    System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);
    writePosition += read;
}
```

The issue is that `toWrite.read(buffer)` returns `Math.min(buffer.length, toWrite.available())`. If `toWrite` has more bytes than the remaining space in `this.bytes`, only `buffer.length` bytes will be copied. But `buffer.length` should be exactly the right size since the buffer was allocated with the correct size.

Hmm, but what if the buffer is a `ReadOnlyArrayData` or `CompositeBufferData`? Let me trace through:

1. In `writeChunked`, `buffer` is a `BufferData` from the application. 
2. `buffer.available()` returns the number of unread bytes.
3. The hex string is created from `available`.
4. A new `FixedBufferData` is created with size `available + hex.length + 4`.
5. We write hex, \r, \n, buffer, \r, \n into the new buffer.

Now, step 5 calls `toWrite.write(buffer)` where `buffer` is the application's buffer. This calls `FixedBufferData.write(BufferData toWrite)`. The remaining capacity is `length - writePosition` which should be `available + 4` (since we wrote `hex.length` bytes for hex and 2 for \r\n before).

Wait, that's not right. Let me recount:
- Initial capacity: `available + hex.length + 4`
- After `write(hex)`: writePosition = `hex.length`
- After `write('\r')` and `write('\n')`: writePosition = `hex.length + 2`
- Remaining capacity: `available + hex.length + 4 - hex.length - 2` = `available + 2`
- After `write(buffer)`: writePosition = `hex.length + 2 + available`
- Remaining capacity: `2`
- After `write('\r')` and `write('\n')`: writePosition = `hex.length + 2 + available + 2` = `hex.length + available + 4`

That looks correct.

But wait, there's an issue with `FixedBufferData.write(BufferData toWrite)`:

```java
public void write(BufferData toWrite) {
    byte[] buffer = new byte[length - writePosition];
    int read = toWrite.read(buffer);
    System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);
    writePosition += read;
}
```

This creates a temporary byte array of size `length - writePosition`, reads from `toWrite` into it, then copies to `this.bytes`. This should be fine.

But let me look at the `FixedBufferData.write(BufferData toWrite, int length)` method:
```java
public void write(BufferData toWrite, int length) {
    byte[] buffer = new byte[length];
    int read = toWrite.read(buffer);
    System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);
    writePosition += read;

```

This is different! It creates a buffer of size `length` and reads `length` bytes from `toWrite`. But it's not called in the writeChunked path.

OK, let me think about this differently. Maybe the issue is not in the chunked encoding itself but in the async writer or the socket write. Let me look at the `SmartSocketWriter` more carefully.

Looking at `SmartSocketWriter`:

```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    if (asyncMode) {
        asyncWriter.write(buffer);
        if (++windowIndex % WINDOW_SIZE == 0 && asyncWriter.avgQueueSize() < QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD) {
            asyncMode = false;
        }
    } else {
        asyncWriter.drainQueue();
        writeNow(buffer);       // blocking write
    }
}
```

When `asyncMode` switches to `false`, it calls `asyncWriter.drainQueue()` and then `writeNow(buffer)`. But there's a race condition! The `asyncWriter` has its own thread that's consuming from the queue. When `asyncMode` becomes false, the `asyncWriter`'s thread might still be running and processing buffers. So `drainQueue()` might not drain all buffers (some might have been consumed by the thread already). And more importantly, the thread might be in the middle of writing a buffer when `drainQueue()` is called.

But wait, `drainQueue()` in `SocketWriterAsync`:
```java
void drainQueue() {
    BufferData buffer;
    while ((buffer = writeQueue.poll()) != null) {
        writeNow(buffer);
    }
}
```

This only drains what's currently in the queue. The async thread might be in the middle of writing a buffer (via `writeNow(toWrite)`) while `drainQueue()` is happening. This could lead to concurrent writes to the same socket!

Actually wait, let me re-read `SocketWriterAsync.run()`:

```java
private void run() {
    this.thread = Thread.currentThread();
    this.thread.setName("[" + socket().socketId() + " " + socket().childSocketId() + "]");
    try {
        while (run) {
            CompositeBufferData toWrite = BufferData.createComposite(writeQueue.take());  // wait if the queue is empty
            int queueSize = 1;
            for (; queueSize <= 1000; queueSize++) {
                BufferData newBuf = writeQueue.poll(); // drain ~all elements from the queue, don't wait.
                if (newBuf == null) {
                    break;
                }
                toWrite.add(newBuf);
            }
            writeNow(toWrite);
            avgQueueSize = (avgQueueSize + queueSize) / 2.0;
        }
        cdl.countDown();
    } catch (Throwable e) {
        this.caught = e;
        this.run = false;
    }
}
```

The loop: take one element from the queue (blocking), then poll up to 1000 more non-blocking, then write via `writeNow`. 

Now in `SmartSocketWriter`:
- When `asyncMode` is true: `asyncWriter.write(buffer)` puts the buffer in the queue.
- When it switches to false: calls `asyncWriter.drainQueue()` and then writes directly.

The problem: after `asyncMode = false`, the async thread could still be running and about to write something. Meanwhile, the main thread calls `drainQueue()` and then `writeNow(buffer)`. The async thread might complete its `writeNow(toWrite)` after `drainQueue()` but before `writeNow(buffer)` - causing ordering issues!

But more importantly, there's a subtle issue in `SocketWriterAsync`: the `run()` method creates a `CompositeBufferData` and writes it. But `CompositeListBufferData` (which is the implementation of `BufferData.createComposite(first)`) doesn't override `writeTo` for the composite case - it falls through to `CompositeListBufferData.writeTo`.

Let me look at this more carefully. Actually, I think the real problem might be in the `CompositeListBufferData.writeTo` method or in how the composite buffer is written via NIO.

Let me look at `CompositeListBufferData.writeTo`:

```java
public int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int limit) {
    int written = 0;
    for (BufferData datum : data) {
        if (datum.consumed()) {
            continue;
        }
        int datumWrote = datum.writeTo(writeBuffer, limit - written);
        if (datumWrote == 0) {
            // not consumed and wrote 0 -> full
            break;
        }
        written += datumWrote;
    }
    return written;
}
```

And `NioSocket.write`:
```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
            writeBuffer.clear();
            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
            writeBuffer.flip();
            delegate.write(writeBuffer);
        }
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

Wait! I see a potential issue. `buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available())` - this should write up to `buffer.available()` bytes. But `buffer.available()` may decrease as we write (since `writeTo` advances read positions). So the `while` loop should work correctly.

But hold on - let me look at the `CompositeArrayBufferData.writeTo`:

```java
public int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int limit) {
    int written = 0;
    for (BufferData datum : data) {
        if (datum.consumed()) {
            continue;
        }
        int datumWrote = datum.writeTo(writeBuffer, limit - written);
        if (datumWrote == 0) {
            // not consumed and wrote 0 -> full
            break;
        }
        written += datumWrote;
    }
    return written;
}
```

This is identical to `CompositeListBufferData.writeTo`. Both look correct.

Let me now think about the `SmartSocketWriter` more carefully. The issue might be a race condition in the switch from async to sync mode.

Actually, let me look at `SocketWriterAsync` again. There's a `close()` method:

```java
public void close() {
    run = false;
    if (!started.get()) {
        // thread never started
        return;
    }
    try {
        writeQueue.put(CLOSING_TOKEN); // wake up blocked take() operation
        if (cdl.await(1000, TimeUnit.MILLISECONDS)) {
            // reads finished because we set run to false
            BufferData available;
            while ((available = writeQueue.poll()) != null) {
                try {
                    writeNow(available);
                } catch (Exception e) {
                    LOGGER.log(System.Logger.Level.TRACE, "Failed to write last buffers during writer shutdown", e);
                }
            }
        }
        if (thread != null) {
            thread.interrupt();
        }
    } catch (InterruptedException e) {
    }
}
```

But this is only called on connection close. 

Now let me look at the problem from a different angle. The PR description says:
- "If using chunked transfer, I occasionally see 'missing CR' or 'Malformed encoding found in chunked-encoding'"
- "If sending content-length header, the transfer occasionally just gets stuck completely"

The "gets stuck completely" with content-length is interesting. Let me look at the `write` method in `BlockingOutputStream` for non-chunked (content-length) case:

```java
if (!isChunked) {
    if (firstByte) {
        firstByte = false;
        Status usedStatus = status.get();
        sendListener.status(ctx, usedStatus);
        sendListener.headers(ctx, headers);
        // write headers and payload part in one buffer to avoid TCP/ACK delay problems
        BufferData growing = BufferData.growing(256 + buffer.available());
        nonEntityBytes(headers, usedStatus, growing, keepAlive, validateHeaders);
        // check not exceeding content-length
        bytesWritten += buffer.available();
        checkContentLength(buffer);
        sendListener.data(ctx, buffer);
        // write single buffer headers and payload part
        growing.write(buffer);
        responseBytesTotal += growing.available();
        dataWriter.write(growing);
    } else {
        // if not chunked, always write
        writeContent(buffer);
    }
    return;
}
```

For the first byte with content-length, it creates a growing buffer, writes headers + payload, then sends it with `dataWriter.write(growing)`. 

For subsequent writes: `writeContent(buffer)` calls `dataWriter.write(buffer)`.

Now, the issue with "gets stuck completely" could happen if the `SmartSocketWriter` or `SocketWriterAsync` has a threading issue. Let me think about this...

Actually, looking at the `SmartSocketWriter` more carefully:

1. `asyncMode` starts as `true`
2. Each write goes to `asyncWriter.write(buffer)` which puts it in a queue
3. Every `WINDOW_SIZE` (1000) writes, it checks `avgQueueSize < 2.0`
4. If yes, it switches to sync mode: `asyncMode = false`
5. In sync mode: `asyncWriter.drainQueue()` then `writeNow(buffer)`

The issue: `avgQueueSize` is computed in the async thread as `(avgQueueSize + queueSize) / 2.0`. But the async thread might be delayed, so `avgQueueSize` might not reflect the current state. More importantly, `windowIndex` is incremented in the calling thread (the HTTP handler thread), while `avgQueueSize` is updated in the async writer thread.

But the real problem I think is about concurrent access. When `asyncMode = false` is set, the calling thread drains the queue and writes directly. But the async thread might still be running and processing its current batch. This could lead to:
1. The async thread writes its composite buffer (from `writeNow(toWrite)`)
2. The main thread drains the queue (grabbing remaining buffers)
3. The main thread writes those drained buffers
4. The main thread writes the current buffer

But the async thread's write might interleave with the main thread's writes! If the async thread is in the middle of `writeNow(toWrite)` when the main thread starts `writeNow(buffer)`, we have concurrent writes to the same socket.

Actually wait, `writeNow` in `SocketWriter`:
```java
public void writeNow(BufferData buffer) {
    socket.write(buffer);
}
```

And `NioSocket.write`:
```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
            writeBuffer.clear();
            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
            writeBuffer.flip();
            delegate.write(writeBuffer);
        }
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

The `writeBuffer` is an instance field, so if two threads call `write` concurrently on the same `NioSocket`, they'd corrupt each other's data! This is the bug!

But wait, is this actually possible? Let me trace through more carefully:

1. Async thread: `writeNow(toWrite)` → `socket.write(toWrite)` → loop
2. Main thread: after `asyncMode = false`, calls `asyncWriter.drainQueue()` which calls `writeNow(buffer)` for each queued buffer → `socket.write(buffer)` → loop
3. Main thread: then calls `writeNow(buffer)` → `socket.write(buffer)` → loop

If step 1 and step 2 happen concurrently, we have two threads writing to the same `NioSocket.writeBuffer` and `delegate`! This would corrupt the data stream.

But actually, there might be a simpler explanation. Let me look at the `SocketWriterAsync`'s `run()` method. When `SmartSocketWriter` switches to sync mode, the `SocketWriterAsync` thread is still running. The `drainQueue()` call might race with the async thread. But even without the race, the `SmartSocketWriter` design seems flawed for concurrent access.

- "If using chunked transfer, I occasionally see 'missing CR' or 'Malformed encoding found in chunked-encoding'"

Let me look at the `SocketWriterAsync.write` method again:

```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    checkRunning();

        if (!writeQueue.offer(buffer, 10, TimeUnit.SECONDS)) {
            checkRunning();

The `checkRunning()` starts the async writer thread on the first write. And `writeQueue.offer(buffer, 10, TimeUnit.SECONDS)` blocks for up to 10 seconds if the queue is full.

```java

        asyncWriter.write(buffer);
        if (++windowIndex % WINDOW_SIZE == 0 && asyncWriter.avgQueueSize() < QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD) {
            asyncMode = false;
        }

Actually, the thread that sets `asyncMode = false` is the only one that can do so (since it's volatile and checked first). But another thread could have just called `asyncWriter.write(buffer)` before the switch, and that buffer is in the queue. `drainQueue()` should pick it up.

But the real issue: after switching to sync mode, the async thread might still be processing. The `drainQueue()` method drains whatever is in the queue at that moment. But the async thread might have taken a buffer from the queue before `drainQueue()` could get it, and is currently writing it. Then after `drainQueue()` returns, the main thread calls `writeNow(buffer)`. These two writes can interleave!

This is the bug! The `SmartSocketWriter` has a race condition where both the async writer thread and the main thread can call `socket.write()` concurrently.

```java

This correctly reads up to `Math.min(length, available)` bytes. Since `buffer.length` equals `available` (from `toWrite`), it should read all bytes.

`BufferData.createComposite(writeQueue.take())` creates a `CompositeListBufferData` with a single element. Then it adds more buffers from the queue. Then writes via `writeNow(toWrite)`.

The `writeNow` calls `NioSocket.write(buffer)`:
```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
            writeBuffer.clear();
            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
            writeBuffer.flip();
            delegate.write(writeBuffer);
        }
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }

For a `CompositeListBufferData`, `buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available())` calls:
```java
public int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int limit) {
    int written = 0;
    for (BufferData datum : data) {
        if (datum.consumed()) {
            continue;
        }
        int datumWrote = datum.writeTo(writeBuffer, limit - written);
        if (datumWrote == 0) {
            break;
        }
        written += datumWrote;

    return written;

```

Wait, there's a potential issue here! When `datum.writeTo(writeBuffer, limit - written)` is called, `limit - written` could be very large (the total available bytes). But `writeBuffer` only has space for `writeBuffer.limit() - writeBuffer.position()` bytes. Let me check each `datum.writeTo`:

For `FixedBufferData`:
```java
public int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int length) {

    toWrite = Math.min(toWrite, length);
    if (toWrite == 0) {
        return 0;
    }

    readPosition += toWrite;

```

This caps at `writeBuffer.limit() - writeBuffer.position()`, which is the remaining space in the write buffer. So it should be fine.

But wait, for `ReadOnlyArrayData`:
```java
public int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int length) {

    toWrite = Math.min(toWrite, length);
    if (toWrite == 0) {
        return 0;
    }
    writeBuffer.put(this.bytes, offset + position, toWrite);
    position += toWrite;
    return toWrite;

Same thing. OK, so the composite buffer write should work correctly.

Now, let me think about the "missing CR" error. The chunk format is:
```
chunk-size CRLF
chunk-data CRLF
```

If the `writeChunked` method writes this correctly, then the corruption must happen somewhere else. Let me think about what could cause "missing CR":

1. The data is written correctly to the buffer
2. The buffer is written to the socket
3. But some bytes are lost or corrupted

Could the `NioSocket.write` method lose data? Let me look:

```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
            writeBuffer.clear();
            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
            writeBuffer.flip();
            delegate.write(writeBuffer);
        }
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

The `delegate.write(writeBuffer)` writes bytes to the socket. `SocketChannel.write(ByteBuffer)` returns the number of bytes written, but this code doesn't check the return value! It assumes all bytes are written. But `SocketChannel.write` may not write all bytes in one call (partial write). 

According to the Java documentation for `SocketChannel.write`:
> Writes a sequence of bytes to this channel from the given buffer. 
> An attempt is made to write up to r bytes to the channel, where r is the number of bytes remaining in the buffer, that is, `src.remaining()`, at the moment this method is invoked.
> ...
> Returns: The number of bytes written, possibly zero

So `SocketChannel.write` may write fewer bytes than `buffer.remaining()`. The code doesn't handle this case! It just calls `delegate.write(writeBuffer)` once and assumes all bytes are written. If the write is partial, some bytes are lost!

Wait, but `SocketChannel` is in blocking mode by default. In blocking mode, `write` should write all bytes (or at least, it should loop internally). Let me check...

Actually, from Java documentation:
> If the channel is in blocking mode, the invocation of this method will block until at least one byte has been written, then return.

So in blocking mode, it should write at least one byte, but it may not write all bytes. However, in practice with TCP, a write of a small buffer (8KB) usually completes fully. But it's not guaranteed!

But this doesn't explain the intermittent nature of the bug. If `SocketChannel.write` returned short, we'd see corruption very frequently for large buffers.

Actually wait, the `writeBuffer` is 8KB. If the chunk size is larger than 8KB, multiple writes are needed. The first write writes the hex + CRLF + first part of data. The second write writes the remaining data + CRLF. This should work correctly because the `while (!buffer.consumed())` loop continues until all bytes are written.

But here's the thing: `writeBuffer.flip()` sets `limit = position` and `position = 0`. Then `delegate.write(writeBuffer)` should write `limit` bytes. But after the write, `writeBuffer` may still have bytes remaining (if the write was partial). The code doesn't check for this! Let me verify:

```java
writeBuffer.clear();     // position=0, limit=capacity
buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());  // writes up to capacity bytes
writeBuffer.flip();      // limit=position, position=0
delegate.write(writeBuffer);  // writes from position to limit
```

After `delegate.write`, if not all bytes were written, `writeBuffer` still has `remaining() > 0`. But the next iteration calls `writeBuffer.clear()`, which sets `position=0, limit=capacity`, discarding any unwritten bytes!

This is a bug! But it would be very noticeable if it happened - you'd lose data on every large write. The fact that the bug is intermittent suggests something else.

Actually, let me check the JDK's behavior. For `SocketChannel` in blocking mode, the `write` method typically writes all remaining bytes. From the JDK source:

Looking at OpenJDK's `SocketChannelImpl.write`:
```java
public int write(ByteBuffer buf) throws IOException {
    ...
    try {
        ...
        do {
            n = IOUtil.write(...);
        } while (n > 0 && buf.hasRemaining());
        return n;
    } ...
}
```

Wait, actually the JDK implementation DOES loop internally for blocking sockets. Let me verify...

Actually, looking at OpenJDK's `IOUtil.write`:
```java
static int write(FileDescriptor fd, ByteBuffer src, ...) throws IOException {
    ...
    int n = writeFromNativeBuffer(fd, ...);
    if (n > 0) {
        src.position(src.position() + n);
    }
    return n;
}
```

And the caller in `SocketChannelImpl`:
```java
public int write(ByteBuffer buf) throws IOException {
    ...
    try {
        ...
        do {
            n = IOUtil.write(fd, buf, -1, ...);
        } while (n > 0 && buf.hasRemaining());
        return n;
    } ...
}
```

So yes, for blocking mode, `SocketChannel.write` loops until all bytes are written (or an error occurs). So the `NioSocket.write` method is correct for blocking sockets.

OK so the socket write itself is fine. Let me reconsider.

Let me look at the `SmartSocketWriter` race condition again. I think this is the real problem:

1. Thread A (HTTP handler): calls `SmartSocketWriter.write(buffer1)` → asyncMode=true, puts buffer1 in queue
2. Thread B (async writer): takes buffer1 from queue, starts writing it via `socket.write(buffer1)`
3. Thread A: calls `SmartSocketWriter.write(buffer2)` → asyncMode=true, puts buffer2 in queue
4. ... this continues for many writes ...
5. At some point, `windowIndex % 1000 == 0` and `avgQueueSize < 2.0`, so `asyncMode = false`
6. Thread A: calls `SmartSocketWriter.write(bufferN)`, asyncMode=false
7. Thread A: calls `asyncWriter.drainQueue()` - drains remaining buffers
8. Thread A: calls `writeNow(bufferN)` - writes directly to socket
9. BUT: Thread B might still be processing its current batch (from step 2 or later batches)

If Thread B is still writing when Thread A starts writing, they'll corrupt each other!

But actually, let me re-examine. `drainQueue()` just polls from the queue. The async thread takes from the queue using `take()` (blocking) and `poll()` (non-blocking). After `drainQueue()` drains everything, Thread B should be blocked on `writeQueue.take()` waiting for the next buffer. But then Thread A writes directly without putting anything in the queue, so Thread B stays blocked.

Wait, but there's a timing issue: what if Thread B is in the middle of `writeNow(toWrite)` when Thread A does `drainQueue()` + `writeNow(bufferN)`? Let me trace:

1. Thread B: `CompositeBufferData toWrite = BufferData.createComposite(writeQueue.take());` - got buffer
2. Thread B: drains more from queue with `poll()`
3. Thread B: `writeNow(toWrite)` - starts writing
4. Thread A: `asyncMode = false`
5. Thread A: `drainQueue()` - polls remaining buffers from queue
6. Thread A: `writeNow(bufferN)` - writes directly
7. Thread B: still in `writeNow(toWrite)` from step 3!

Both threads are writing to the same socket concurrently! The `NioSocket.write` uses an instance-level `writeBuffer` that would be corrupted by concurrent access.

This is the bug! The `SmartSocketWriter` has a race condition where both the async writer thread and the calling thread can write to the socket concurrently.

But wait, in step 5, Thread A drains the queue. The queue is an `ArrayBlockingQueue`. After draining, Thread B's next `take()` would block. But Thread B is currently in `writeNow(toWrite)`, which doesn't interact with the queue. So the race is real.

Now, the fix should ensure that when switching from async to sync mode, the async writer thread is properly stopped before any direct writes occur.

But let me also consider: is the `SmartSocketWriter` always used? Looking at `ConnectionHandler`:

```java
writer = SocketWriter.create(listenerContext.executor(),
                             helidonSocket,
                             listenerConfig.writeQueueLength(),
                             listenerConfig.smartAsyncWrites());
```

Default values for these configs would determine which writer is used. Let me check the defaults:</think>Let me check the configuration defaults for the writer

So the defaults are:
- `writeQueueLength`: 0 (meaning direct writes, `SocketWriterDirect` is used)
- `smartAsyncWrites`: false

With `writeQueueLength = 0`, `SocketWriter.create` returns `SocketWriterDirect` (since `0 <= 1`). So by default, async writes are NOT used. The `SmartSocketWriter` is only used when both `writeQueueLength > 1` and `smartAsyncWrites = true`.

But the bug report says the issue occurs. Maybe they have configured async writes? Or maybe the issue is elsewhere?

Let me re-examine the problem. The `SocketWriterDirect` is used by default:
```java
class SocketWriterDirect extends SocketWriter implements DataWriter {
    SocketWriterDirect(HelidonSocket socket) {
        super(socket);
    }

    @Override
    public void write(BufferData... buffers) {
        writeNow(buffers);
    }

    @Override
    public void write(BufferData buffer) {
        writeNow(buffer);
    }
}
```

And `writeNow` calls `socket.write(buffer)` which is the `NioSocket.write` we analyzed. This is a straightforward synchronous write.

OK so the `SmartSocketWriter` is likely not the issue (since it's disabled by default). Let me look at this from a different angle.

Let me look at the `BufferedOutputStream` used in `ClosingBufferedOutputStream`:

```java
ClosingBufferedOutputStream(BlockingOutputStream out, int size) {
    this.closingDelegate = out;
    this.delegate = size <= 0 ? out : new BufferedOutputStream(out, size);
}
```

The default `writeBufferSize` is 4096. So there's a `BufferedOutputStream` wrapping the `BlockingOutputStream`. The `BufferedOutputStream` buffers writes and flushes them to the underlying stream when the buffer is full or when `flush()` is called.

Now, look at `ClosingBufferedOutputStream.close()`:
```java
@Override
public void close() {
    closingDelegate.closing();     // inform of imminent call to close for last flush
    try {
        delegate.close();
    } catch (IOException | UncheckedIOException e) {
        throw new ServerConnectionException("Failed to close server output stream", e);
    }
}
```

And `ClosingBufferedOutputStream.commit()`:
```java
void commit() {
    try {
        flush();
        closingDelegate.commit();
    } catch (IOException | UncheckedIOException e) {
        throw new ServerConnectionException("Failed to flush server output stream", e);
    }
}
```

Wait, `commit()` calls `flush()` then `closingDelegate.commit()`. But when? Let me look at the flow from the user's perspective:

1. User gets `outputStream()` and writes data to it
2. When the user closes the output stream (or the try-with-resources closes it), `close()` is called
3. `close()` calls `closingDelegate.closing()` then `delegate.close()` which flushes the `BufferedOutputStream` then calls `BlockingOutputStream.close()` (which is a no-op)

But `commit()` is never called in this flow! Let me check where `commit()` is called:</think>Let me search for where `commit()` is called on the response:

    21	import java.util.List;
    22	import java.util.Map;
    23	import java.util.concurrent.Callable;
    24	import java.util.function.Supplier;

    26	import io.helidon.common.Weights;
    27	import io.helidon.http.DirectHandler;
    28	import io.helidon.http.HttpException;
    29	import io.helidon.http.HttpPrologue;
    30	import io.helidon.http.NotFoundException;
    31	import io.helidon.http.RequestException;
    32	import io.helidon.http.Status;

    34	import io.helidon.webserver.ServerLifecycle;

    36	
    37	final class HttpRoutingImpl implements HttpRouting {
    38	    private static final System.Logger LOGGER = System.getLogger(HttpRoutingImpl.class.getName());
    39	    private static final HttpRoutingImpl EMPTY = builder().build();
    40	
    41	    private final Filters filters;
    42	    private final ServiceRoute rootRoute;
    43	    private final List<HttpFeature> features;
    44	    private final int maxReRouteCount;
    45	    private final HttpSecurity security;
    46	
    47	    HttpRoutingImpl(RealBuilder builder) {
    48	        ErrorHandlers errorHandlers = ErrorHandlers.create(builder.errorHandlers);
    49	        this.filters = Filters.create(errorHandlers, List.copyOf(builder.filters));
    50	        this.rootRoute = builder.rootRules.build();
    51	        this.features = List.copyOf(builder.features);
    52	        this.maxReRouteCount = builder.maxReRouteCount;
    53	        this.security = builder.security;
    54	    }
    55	
    56	    static BuilderImpl builder() {
    57	        return new BuilderImpl();
    58	    }
    59	
    60	    /**
    61	     * Empty routing (all requests will return {@link Status#NOT_FOUND_404}.
    62	     *
    63	     * @return empty routing
    64	     */
    65	    static HttpRoutingImpl empty() {
    66	        return EMPTY;
    67	    }
    68	
    69	    @Override
    70	    public void route(ConnectionContext ctx, RoutingRequest request, RoutingResponse response) {
    71	        RoutingExecutor routingExecutor = new RoutingExecutor(ctx, rootRoute, request, response, maxReRouteCount);
    72	        // we cannot throw an exception to the filters, as then the filter would not have information about actual status
    73	        // code, so error handling is done in routing executor and for each filter
    74	        filters.filter(ctx, request, response, routingExecutor);
    75	    }
    76	
    77	    @Override
    78	    public void beforeStart() {
    79	        filters.beforeStart();
    80	        rootRoute.beforeStart();
    81	        features.forEach(ServerLifecycle::beforeStart);
    82	    }
    83	
    84	    @Override
    85	    public void afterStart(WebServer webServer) {
    86	        filters.afterStart(webServer);
    87	        rootRoute.afterStart(webServer);
    88	        features.forEach(f -> f.afterStart(webServer));
    89	    }
    90	
    91	    @Override
    92	    public void afterStop() {
    93	        filters.afterStop();
    94	        rootRoute.afterStop();
    95	        features.forEach(ServerLifecycle::afterStop);
    96	    }
    97	
    98	    @Override
    99	    public HttpSecurity security() {
   100	        return security;
   101	    }
   102	
   103	
   104	    private enum RoutingResult {
   105	        ROUTE,
   106	        FINISH,
   107	        NONE
   108	    }
   109	
   110	    private static final class RoutingExecutor implements Callable<Void> {
   111	        private final ConnectionContext ctx;
   112	        private final RoutingRequest request;
   113	        private final RoutingResponse response;
   114	        private final ServiceRoute rootRoute;
   115	        private final int maxReRouteCount;
   116	
   117	        private RoutingExecutor(ConnectionContext ctx,
   118	                                ServiceRoute rootRoute,
   119	                                RoutingRequest request,
   120	                                RoutingResponse response,
   121	                                int maxReRouteCount) {
   122	            this.ctx = ctx;
   123	            this.rootRoute = rootRoute;
   124	            this.request = request;
   125	            this.response = response;
   126	            this.maxReRouteCount = maxReRouteCount;
   127	        }
   128	
   129	        @Override
   130	        public Void call() throws Exception {
   131	            // initial attempt - most common case, handled separately
   132	            RoutingResult result = doRoute(ctx, request, response);
   133	
   134	            if (result == RoutingResult.FINISH) {
   135	                response.commit();
   136	                return null;
   137	            }
   138	            if (result == RoutingResult.NONE) {
   139	                throw new NotFoundException("Endpoint not found");
   140	            }
   141	
   142	            // rerouting, do the more heavyweight while loop
   143	            int counter = 1;
   144	            while (result == RoutingResult.ROUTE) {
   145	                counter++;
   146	                if (counter == maxReRouteCount) {
   147	                    LOGGER.log(System.Logger.Level.ERROR, "Rerouted more than " + maxReRouteCount
   148	                            + " times. Will not attempt further routing");
   149	
   150	                    throw new HttpException("Too many reroutes", Status.INTERNAL_SERVER_ERROR_500, true);
   151	                }
   152	
   153	                result = doRoute(ctx, request, response);
   154	            }
   155	
   156	            // finished and done
   157	            if (result == RoutingResult.FINISH) {
   158	                response.commit();
   159	                return null;
   160	            }
   161	            throw new NotFoundException("Endpoint not found");
   162	        }
   163	
   164	        private RoutingResult doRoute(ConnectionContext ctx, RoutingRequest request, RoutingResponse response) throws Exception {
   165	            HttpPrologue prologue = request.prologue();
   166	            RouteCrawler crawler = rootRoute.crawler(ctx, request);
   167	
   168	            while (crawler.hasNext()) {
   169	                response.resetRouting();
   170	                RouteCrawler.CrawlerItem next = crawler.next();
   171	                request.path(next.path());
   172	                request.matchingPattern(next.matchingElement());
   173	
   174	                next.handler().handle(request, response);
   175	                if (response.shouldReroute()) {
   176	                    if (response.isSent()) {
   177	                        LOGGER.log(System.Logger.Level.WARNING, "Request to " + request.prologue()
   178	                                + " in inconsistent state. Request to re-route, but response was already sent. Ignoring "
   179	                                + "reroute.");
   180	                        return RoutingResult.FINISH;
   181	                    }
   182	                    HttpPrologue newPrologue = response.reroutePrologue(prologue);
   183	                    request.prologue(newPrologue);
   184	                    response.resetRouting();
   185	                    return RoutingResult.ROUTE;
   186	                }
   187	                if (response.isNexted()) {
   188	                    if (response.isSent()) {
   189	                        LOGGER.log(System.Logger.Level.WARNING, "Request to " + request.prologue()
   190	                                + " in inconsistent state. Request to next, but response was already sent. "
   191	                                + "Ignoring next().");
   192	                        return RoutingResult.FINISH;
   193	                    }
   194	                    continue;
   195	                }
   196	                if (response.hasEntity()) {
   197	                    return RoutingResult.FINISH;
   198	                }
   199	
   200	                // not nexted, not rerouted - invalid state
   201	                // user must send a response within the current thread
   202	                LOGGER.log(System.Logger.Level.WARNING,
   203	                           "A route MUST call either send, reroute, or next on ServerResponse on the request thread. "
   204	                                   + "Neither of these was called for request: " + request.prologue()
   205	                                   + "; Handler: " + next.handler());
   206	
   207	                throw RequestException.builder()
   208	                        // we cannot share the information above with a client
   209	                        .message("Internal Server Error")
   210	                        .type(DirectHandler.EventType.INTERNAL_ERROR)
   211	                        .build();
   212	            }
   213	
   214	            return RoutingResult.NONE;
   215	        }
   216	    }
   217	
   218	
   219	    private static class BuilderImpl implements Builder {
   220	        // collects features, before build, these will be ordered by weight and registered
   221	        private final List<HttpFeature> features = new ArrayList<>();
   222	        private final HttpRoutingFeature mainRouting = new HttpRoutingFeature();
   223	        private HttpSecurity security = HttpSecurity.create();
   224	        private int maxReRouteCount = 10;
   225	
   226	        private BuilderImpl() {
   227	        }
   228	
   229	        private BuilderImpl(List<HttpFeature> features, HttpRoutingFeature mainRouting, HttpSecurity security, int maxReroute) {
   230	            this.features.addAll(features);
   231	            this.mainRouting.copyFrom(mainRouting);
   232	            this.security = security;
   233	            this.maxReRouteCount = maxReroute;
   234	        }
   235	
   236	        @Override
   237	        public HttpRoutingImpl build() {
   238	            if (!features.contains(mainRouting)) {
   239	                features.add(mainRouting);
   240	            }
   241	
   242	            Weights.sort(features);
   243	
   244	            RealBuilder realBuilder = new RealBuilder(features,
   245	                security,
   246	                maxReRouteCount);
   247	
   248	            // now we need to do the final setup in the correct order
   249	            for (HttpFeature feature : features) {
   250	                if (LOGGER.isLoggable(System.Logger.Level.TRACE)) {
   251	                    LOGGER.log(System.Logger.Level.TRACE, "Setting up feature: " + feature.getClass().getName());
   252	                }
   253	                feature.setup(realBuilder);
   254	            }
   255	
   256	            return new HttpRoutingImpl(realBuilder);
   257	        }
   258	
   259	        @Override
   260	        public Builder register(HttpService... service) {
   261	            mainRouting.service(service);
   262	            return this;
   263	        }
   264	
   265	        @Override
   266	        public Builder register(String path, HttpService... service) {
   267	            mainRouting.service(path, service);
   268	            return this;
   269	        }
   270	
   271	        @Override
   272	        public Builder route(HttpRoute route) {
   273	            mainRouting.route(route);
   274	            return this;
   275	        }
   276	
   277	        @Override
   278	        public Builder addFilter(Filter filter) {
   279	            mainRouting.filter(filter);
   280	            return this;
   281	        }
   282	
   283	        @Override
   284	        public Builder addFeature(Supplier<? extends HttpFeature> feature) {
   285	            HttpFeature httpFeature = feature.get();
   286	            features.add(httpFeature);
   287	            return this;
   288	        }
   289	
   290	        @Override
   291	        public <T extends Throwable> Builder error(Class<T> exceptionClass, ErrorHandler<? super T> handler) {
   292	            mainRouting.error(exceptionClass, handler);
   293	            return this;
   294	        }
   295	
   296	        @Override
   297	        public Builder maxReRouteCount(int maxReRouteCount) {
   298	            this.maxReRouteCount = maxReRouteCount;
   299	            return this;
   300	        }
   301	
   302	        @Override
   303	        public Builder security(HttpSecurity security) {
   304	            this.security = security;
   305	            return this;
   306	        }
   307	
   308	        @Override
   309	        public Builder copy() {
   310	            return new BuilderImpl(features, mainRouting, security, maxReRouteCount);
   311	        }
   312	    }
   313	
   314	    private static final class RealBuilder implements Builder {
   315	        private final List<Filter> filters = new ArrayList<>();
   316	        private final Map<Class<? extends Throwable>, ErrorHandler<?>> errorHandlers = new IdentityHashMap<>();
   317	        private final ServiceRules rootRules = new ServiceRules();
   318	        private final List<HttpFeature> features;
   319	
   320	        private HttpSecurity security;
   321	        private int maxReRouteCount;
   322	
   323	        private RealBuilder(List<HttpFeature> features,
   324	            HttpSecurity security,
   325	            int maxReRouteCount) {
   326	
   327	            // we need a new instance, as features may add additional features
   328	            this.features = new ArrayList<>(features);
   329	            this.security = security;
   330	            this.maxReRouteCount = maxReRouteCount;
   331	        }
   332	
   333	        @Override
   334	        public HttpRouting build() {
   335	            throw new UnsupportedOperationException("This builder is internal and never built");
   336	        }
   337	
   338	        @Override
   339	        public Builder register(HttpService... service) {
   340	            rootRules.register(service);
   341	            return this;
   342	        }
   343	
   344	        @Override
   345	        public Builder register(String pathPattern, HttpService... service) {
   346	            rootRules.register(pathPattern, service);
   347	            return this;
   348	        }
   349	
   350	        @Override
   351	        public Builder route(HttpRoute route) {
   352	            rootRules.route(route);
   353	            return this;
   354	        }
   355	
   356	        @Override
   357	        public Builder addFilter(Filter filter) {
   358	            filters.add(filter);
   359	            return this;
   360	        }
   361	
   362	        @Override
   363	        public Builder addFeature(Supplier<? extends HttpFeature> feature) {
   364	            HttpFeature it = feature.get();
   365	            features.add(it);
   366	            it.setup(this);
   367	            return this;
   368	        }
   369	
   370	        @Override
   371	        public <T extends Throwable> Builder error(Class<T> exceptionClass, ErrorHandler<? super T> handler) {
   372	            errorHandlers.putIfAbsent(exceptionClass, handler);
   373	            return this;
   374	        }
   375	
   376	        @Override
   377	        public Builder maxReRouteCount(int maxReRouteCount) {
   378	            this.maxReRouteCount = maxReRouteCount;
   379	            return this;
   380	        }
   381	
   382	        @Override
   383	        public Builder security(HttpSecurity security) {
   384	            this.security = security;
   385	            return this;
   386	        }
   387	
   388	        @Override
   389	        public Builder copy() {
   390	            throw new UnsupportedOperationException("This builder should only be used internally by Helidon and never copied");
   391	        }
   392	    }
   393	}
