    17	package io.helidon.webserver.http;
    18	
    19	import java.io.ByteArrayOutputStream;
    20	import java.io.IOException;
    21	import java.io.OutputStream;
    22	import java.util.ArrayList;
    23	import java.util.List;
    24	import java.util.function.Consumer;
    25	
    26	import io.helidon.common.GenericType;
    27	import io.helidon.common.buffers.BufferData;
    28	import io.helidon.common.uri.UriPath;
    29	import io.helidon.common.uri.UriQuery;
    30	import io.helidon.http.Header;
    31	import io.helidon.http.HeaderName;
    32	import io.helidon.http.HeaderNames;
    33	import io.helidon.http.HeaderValues;
    34	import io.helidon.http.HttpException;
    35	import io.helidon.http.HttpPrologue;
    36	import io.helidon.http.ServerRequestHeaders;
    37	import io.helidon.http.ServerResponseTrailers;
    38	import io.helidon.http.Status;
    39	import io.helidon.http.encoding.ContentEncoder;
    40	import io.helidon.http.encoding.ContentEncodingContext;
    41	import io.helidon.http.media.EntityWriter;
    42	import io.helidon.http.media.InstanceWriter;
    43	import io.helidon.http.media.MediaContext;
    44	import io.helidon.http.media.UnsupportedTypeException;
    45	import io.helidon.webserver.ConnectionContext;
    46	import io.helidon.webserver.ServerConnectionException;
    47	
    48	/**
    49	 * Base class for common server response tasks that can be shared across HTTP versions.
    50	 *
    51	 * @param <T> type of the response extending this class to allow fluent API
    52	 */
    53	@SuppressWarnings("unchecked")
    54	public abstract class ServerResponseBase<T extends ServerResponseBase<T>> implements RoutingResponse {
    55	
    56	    /**
    57	     * Stream result trailer name.
    58	     */
    59	    protected static final HeaderName STREAM_RESULT_NAME = HeaderNames.create("stream-result");
    60	    /**
    61	     * Stream result OK.
    62	     */
    63	    protected static final Header STREAM_RESULT_OK = HeaderValues.create(STREAM_RESULT_NAME, "OK");
    64	
    65	    /**
    66	     * Stream status trailers.
    67	     */
    68	    protected static final Header STREAM_TRAILERS =
    69	            HeaderValues.create(HeaderNames.TRAILER, STREAM_RESULT_NAME.defaultCase());
    70	    private final ContentEncodingContext contentEncodingContext;
    71	    private final MediaContext mediaContext;
    72	    private final ServerRequestHeaders requestHeaders;
    73	    private final List<Runnable> beforeSend = new ArrayList<>(5);
    74	    private final List<Runnable> whenSent = new ArrayList<>(5);
    75	    private final int maxInMemory;
    76	
    77	    private Status status;
    78	    private boolean nexted;
    79	    private boolean reroute;
    80	    private UriQuery rerouteQuery;
    81	    private String reroutePath;
    82	    private Consumer<ServerResponseTrailers> beforeTrailers;
    83	
    84	    /**
    85	     * Create server response.
    86	     *
    87	     * @param ctx     context
    88	     * @param request server request
    89	     */
    90	    protected ServerResponseBase(ConnectionContext ctx, ServerRequest request) {
    91	        this.contentEncodingContext = ctx.listenerContext().contentEncodingContext();
    92	        this.mediaContext = ctx.listenerContext().mediaContext();
    93	        this.requestHeaders = request.headers();
    94	        this.maxInMemory = ctx.listenerContext().config().maxInMemoryEntity();
    95	    }
    96	
    97	    @Override
    98	    public T status(Status status) {
    99	        if (isSent()) {
   100	            throw new IllegalStateException("Response already sent");
   101	        }
   102	        this.status = status;
   103	        return (T) this;
   104	    }
   105	
   106	    @Override
   107	    public Status status() {
   108	        if (status == null) {
   109	            return Status.OK_200;
   110	        }
   111	        return status;
   112	    }
   113	
   114	    @Override
   115	    public void send() {
   116	        send(BufferData.EMPTY_BYTES);
   117	    }
   118	
   119	    @Override
   120	    public void send(Object entity) {
   121	        if (entity instanceof byte[] bytes) {
   122	            send(bytes);
   123	            return;
   124	        }
   125	
   126	        try {
   127	            // now we have to use a media writer, so we may fail
   128	            doSend(entity);
   129	        } catch (UnsupportedTypeException e) {
   130	            throw new HttpException(e.getMessage(), Status.UNSUPPORTED_MEDIA_TYPE_415, e, true);
   131	        }
   132	    }
   133	
   134	    @Override
   135	    public ServerResponse beforeSend(Runnable listener) {
   136	        beforeSend.add(listener);
   137	        return (T) this;
   138	    }
   139	
   140	    @Override
   141	    public T whenSent(Runnable listener) {
   142	        whenSent.add(listener);
   143	        return (T) this;
   144	    }
   145	
   146	    @Override
   147	    public T reroute(String newPath) {
   148	        if (nexted) {
   149	            throw new IllegalStateException("Cannot reroute a response that has been nexted");
   150	        }
   151	        this.reroute = true;
   152	        this.reroutePath = newPath;
   153	        return (T) this;
   154	    }
   155	
   156	    @Override
   157	    public T reroute(String path, UriQuery query) {
   158	        if (nexted) {
   159	            throw new IllegalStateException("Cannot reroute a response that has been nexted");
   160	        }
   161	        this.reroute = true;
   162	        this.reroutePath = path;
   163	        this.rerouteQuery = query;
   164	        return (T) this;
   165	    }
   166	
   167	    @Override
   168	    public T next() {
   169	        if (reroute) {
   170	            throw new IllegalStateException("Cannot next a response that has been rerouted");
   171	        }
   172	        this.nexted = true;
   173	        return (T) this;
   174	    }
   175	
   176	    @Override
   177	    public void resetRouting() {
   178	        this.nexted = false;
   179	        this.reroute = false;
   180	        this.reroutePath = null;
   181	        this.rerouteQuery = null;
   182	    }
   183	
   184	    @Override
   185	    public boolean shouldReroute() {
   186	        return reroute;
   187	    }
   188	
   189	    @Override
   190	    public HttpPrologue reroutePrologue(HttpPrologue prologue) {
   191	        return HttpPrologue.create(prologue.rawProtocol(),
   192	                                   prologue.protocol(),
   193	                                   prologue.protocolVersion(),
   194	                                   prologue.method(),
   195	                                   UriPath.create(reroutePath),
   196	                                   rerouteQuery == null ? prologue.query() : rerouteQuery,
   197	                                   prologue.fragment());
   198	    }
   199	
   200	    @Override
   201	    public boolean isNexted() {
   202	        return nexted;
   203	    }
   204	
   205	    @Override
   206	    public ServerResponse beforeTrailers(Consumer<ServerResponseTrailers> beforeTrailers) {
   207	        this.beforeTrailers = beforeTrailers;
   208	        return this;
   209	    }
   210	
   211	    /**
   212	     * Gets consumer for server response trailers if registered on this response.
   213	     *
   214	     * @return consumer if registered or {@code null} otherwise
   215	     */
   216	    protected Consumer<ServerResponseTrailers> beforeTrailers() {
   217	        return beforeTrailers;
   218	    }
   219	
   220	    /**
   221	     * Gets media context for this response.
   222	     *
   223	     * @return the media context
   224	     */
   225	    protected MediaContext mediaContext() {
   226	        return mediaContext;
   227	    }
   228	
   229	    /**
   230	     * Entity bytes encoded using content encoding. Does not attempt encoding
   231	     * if entity is empty.
   232	     *
   233	     * @param configuredEntity plain bytes
   234	     * @return encoded bytes or same entity array if encoding is disabled
   235	     */
   236	    protected byte[] entityBytes(byte[] configuredEntity) {
   237	        return entityBytes(configuredEntity, 0, configuredEntity.length);
   238	    }
   239	
   240	    /**
   241	     * Entity bytes encoded using content encoding. Does not attempt encoding
   242	     * if entity is empty.
   243	     *
   244	     * @param configuredEntity plain bytes
   245	     * @param position starting position
   246	     * @param length number of bytes
   247	     * @return encoded bytes or same entity array if encoding is disabled
   248	     */
   249	    protected byte[] entityBytes(byte[] configuredEntity, int position, int length) {
   250	        byte[] entity = configuredEntity;
   251	        if (contentEncodingContext.contentEncodingEnabled() && length > 0) {
   252	            ContentEncoder encoder = contentEncodingContext.encoder(requestHeaders);
   253	            // we want to preserve optimization here, let's create a new byte array
   254	            ByteArrayOutputStream baos = new ByteArrayOutputStream(length);
   255	            OutputStream os = encoder.apply(baos);
   256	            try {
   257	                os.write(entity, position, length);
   258	                os.close();
   259	            } catch (IOException e) {
   260	                throw new ServerConnectionException("Failed to write response", e);
   261	            }
   262	            entity = baos.toByteArray();
   263	            encoder.headers(headers());
   264	        }
   265	        return entity;
   266	    }
   267	
   268	    /**
   269	     * Encode content using requested/default content encoder.
   270	     *
   271	     * @param outputStream output stream to write encoded data to
   272	     * @return output stream to write plain data to
   273	     */
   274	    protected OutputStream contentEncode(OutputStream outputStream) {
   275	        if (contentEncodingContext.contentEncodingEnabled() && !headers().contains(HeaderNames.CONTENT_ENCODING)) {
   276	            ContentEncoder encoder = contentEncodingContext.encoder(requestHeaders);
   277	            encoder.headers(headers());
   278	
   279	            return encoder.apply(outputStream);
   280	        }
   281	        return outputStream;
   282	    }
   283	
   284	    /**
   285	     * Execute before send runnables.
   286	     */
   287	    protected void beforeSend() {
   288	        beforeSend.forEach(Runnable::run);
   289	    }
   290	
   291	    /**
   292	     * Execute after send runnables.
   293	     */
   294	    protected void afterSend() {
   295	        for (Runnable runnable : whenSent) {
   296	            runnable.run();
   297	        }
   298	    }
   299	
   300	    @SuppressWarnings({"rawtypes", "unchecked"})
   301	    private void doSend(Object entity) {
   302	        GenericType type;
   303	        if (entity instanceof String) {
   304	            type = GenericType.STRING;
   305	        } else {
   306	            type = GenericType.create(entity);
   307	        }
   308	
   309	        EntityWriter writer = mediaContext.writer(type, requestHeaders, headers());
   310	        long configuredContentLength = headers().contentLength().orElse(-1);
   311	        if (writer.supportsInstanceWriter()) {
   312	            InstanceWriter instanceWriter = writer.instanceWriter(type, entity, requestHeaders, headers());
   313	            if (instanceWriter.alwaysInMemory()) {
   314	                send(instanceWriter.instanceBytes());
   315	                return;
   316	            }
   317	            long contentLength = instanceWriter.contentLength().orElse(configuredContentLength);
   318	            if (contentLength != -1 && contentLength < maxInMemory) {
   319	                send(instanceWriter.instanceBytes());
   320	                return;
   321	            }
   322	            instanceWriter.write(outputStream());
   323	            return;
   324	        }
   325	
   326	
   327	        if (configuredContentLength == -1 || configuredContentLength > maxInMemory) {
   328	            OutputStream outputStream = outputStream();
   329	            writer.write(type, entity, outputStream, requestHeaders, this.headers());
   330	            return;
   331	        }
   332	
   333	        // safe to cast to int, as the maxInMemoryEntity configuration option is an int
   334	        ByteArrayOutputStream baos = new ByteArrayOutputStream((int) configuredContentLength);
   335	        writer.write(type, entity, baos, requestHeaders, headers());
   336	        send(baos.toByteArray());
   337	    }
   338	}

    17	package io.helidon.webserver.http;
    18	
    19	import java.net.SocketException;
    20	import java.util.IdentityHashMap;
    21	import java.util.Map;
    22	import java.util.Optional;
    23	import java.util.concurrent.Callable;
    24	
    25	import io.helidon.http.BadRequestException;

    33	import io.helidon.webserver.ServerConnectionException;
    34	
    35	/**
    36	 * Http routing Error handlers.
    37	 */
    38	public final class ErrorHandlers {
    39	    private static final System.Logger LOGGER = System.getLogger(ErrorHandlers.class.getName());
    40	    private final IdentityHashMap<Class<? extends Throwable>, ErrorHandler<?>> errorHandlers;
    41	
    42	    private ErrorHandlers(IdentityHashMap<Class<? extends Throwable>, ErrorHandler<?>> errorHandlers) {
    43	        this.errorHandlers = errorHandlers;
    44	    }
    45	
    46	    /**
    47	     * Create error handlers.
    48	     *
    49	     * @param errorHandlers map of type to error handler
    50	     * @return new error handlers
    51	     */
    52	    public static ErrorHandlers create(Map<Class<? extends Throwable>, ErrorHandler<?>> errorHandlers) {
    53	        return new ErrorHandlers(new IdentityHashMap<>(errorHandlers));
    54	    }
    55	
    56	    @Override
    57	    public String toString() {
    58	        return "ErrorHandlers for " + errorHandlers.keySet();
    59	    }
    60	
    61	    /**
    62	     * Run a task and handle the errors, if any. Uses error handlers configured on routing.
    63	     * Correctly handles all expected (and unexpected) exceptions that can happen in filters and routes.
    64	     *
    65	     * @param ctx      connection context
    66	     * @param request  HTTP server request
    67	     * @param response HTTP server response
    68	     * @param task     task to execute
    69	     */
    70	    @SuppressWarnings({"unchecked", "rawtypes"})
    71	    public void runWithErrorHandling(ConnectionContext ctx,
    72	                                     RoutingRequest request,
    73	                                     RoutingResponse response,
    74	                                     Callable<Void> task) {
    75	        try {
    76	            task.call();
    77	            if (response.hasEntity()) {
    78	                response.commit();
    79	            }
    80	        } catch (CloseConnectionException e) {
    81	            // these errors must "bubble up"
    82	            throw e;
    83	        } catch (RequestException e) {
    84	            handleRequestException(ctx, request, response, e);
    85	        } catch (InternalServerException e) {
    86	            // this is the place error handling must be done
    87	            // check if error handler exists for cause - if so, use it
    88	            ErrorHandler errorHandler = null;
    89	            Throwable exception = null;
    90	
    91	            if (e.getCause() != null) {
    92	                var maybeEh = errorHandler(e.getCause().getClass());
    93	                if (maybeEh.isPresent()) {
    94	                    errorHandler = maybeEh.get();
    95	                    exception = e.getCause();
    96	                }
    97	            }
    98	
    99	            if (errorHandler == null) {
   100	                errorHandler = errorHandler(e.getClass()).orElse(null);
   101	                exception = e;
   102	            }
   103	
   104	            if (errorHandler == null) {
   105	                unhandledError(ctx, request, response, exception);
   106	            } else {
   107	                handleError(ctx, request, response, exception, errorHandler);
   108	            }
   109	        } catch (RuntimeException e) {
   110	            // this handles also all HttpException instances, including BadRequestException, as this was thrown
   111	            // from routing, where we already have a full request and response, so we can handle it in user's error handler
   112	            // it only re-throws the BadRequestException if there is no user handler for it
   113	            handleError(ctx, request, response, e);
   114	        } catch (Throwable e) {
   115	            if (e.getCause() instanceof SocketException se) {
   116	                throw new ServerConnectionException("SocketException during routing", se);
   117	            }
   118	            handleError(ctx, request, response, e);
   119	        }
   120	    }
   121	
   122	    @SuppressWarnings("unchecked")
   123	    <T extends Throwable> Optional<ErrorHandler<T>> errorHandler(Class<T> exceptionClass) {
   124	        // then look for error handlers that handle supertypes of this exception from lower to higher
   125	        Class<? extends Throwable> throwableClass = exceptionClass;
   126	        while (true) {
   127	            // first look for exact match
   128	            ErrorHandler<?> errorHandler = errorHandlers.get(throwableClass);
   129	            if (errorHandler != null) {
   130	                return Optional.of((ErrorHandler<T>) errorHandler);
   131	            }
   132	            if (!Throwable.class.isAssignableFrom(throwableClass)) {
   133	                return Optional.empty();
   134	            }
   135	            if (throwableClass == Throwable.class) {
   136	                return Optional.empty();
   137	            }
   138	            throwableClass = (Class<? extends Throwable>) throwableClass.getSuperclass();
   139	        }
   140	    }
   141	
   142	    private void handleRequestException(ConnectionContext ctx,
   143	                                        ServerRequest request,
   144	                                        RoutingResponse response,
   145	                                        RequestException e) {
   146	        // we are only interested in resetting the streams, headers are at the discretion of the error handler
   147	        if (!response.resetStream()) {
   148	            ctx.log(LOGGER, System.Logger.Level.WARNING,
   149	                    "Request failed: %s, cannot send error response, as response already sent",
   150	                    e, request.prologue());
   151	            throw new CloseConnectionException(
   152	                    "Cannot send response of an error handler, status and headers already written");
   153	        }
   154	        boolean keepAlive = e.keepAlive();
   155	        if (keepAlive && !request.content().consumed()) {
   156	            // there is a chance, that the 100-Continue was already sent! In such a case, we MUST consume entity
   157	            if (request.headers().contains(HeaderValues.EXPECT_100) && !request.continueSent()) {
   158	                // No content is coming, reset connection
   159	                request.reset();
   160	            } else {
   161	                try {
   162	                    // attempt to consume the request entity (only when keeping the connection alive)
   163	                    request.content().consume();
   164	                } catch (Exception _) {
   165	                    keepAlive = request.content().consumed();
   166	                }
   167	            }
   168	        }
   169	        ctx.listenerContext()
   170	                .directHandlers()
   171	                .handle(e, response, keepAlive);
   172	
   173	        response.commit();
   174	    }
   175	
   176	    @SuppressWarnings("unchecked")
   177	    private void handleError(ConnectionContext ctx, RoutingRequest request, RoutingResponse response, Throwable e) {
   178	        errorHandler(e.getClass())
   179	                .ifPresentOrElse(it -> handleError(ctx, request, response, e, (ErrorHandler<Throwable>) it),
   180	                                 () -> unhandledError(ctx, request, response, e));
   181	    }
   182	
   183	    private void unhandledError(ConnectionContext ctx, ServerRequest request, RoutingResponse response, Throwable e) {
   184	        if (e instanceof BadRequestException bre) {
   185	            // maybe there is a direct handler for this exception, falling back to original behavior
   186	            throw bre;
   187	        }
   188	        if (e instanceof HttpException httpException) {
   189	            handleRequestException(ctx, request, response, RequestException.builder()
   190	                    .cause(e)
   191	                    .type(DirectHandler.EventType.OTHER)
   192	                    .message(e.getMessage())
   193	                    .status(httpException.status())
   194	                    .setKeepAlive(httpException.keepAlive())
   195	                    .request(DirectTransportRequest.create(request.prologue(), request.headers()))
   196	                    .update(it -> httpException.headers().forEach(it::header))
   197	                    .build());
   198	        } else {
   199	            // to be handled by error handler
   200	            handleRequestException(ctx, request, response, RequestException.builder()
   201	                    .cause(e)
   202	                    .type(DirectHandler.EventType.INTERNAL_ERROR)
   203	                    .message(e.getMessage())
   204	                    .request(DirectTransportRequest.create(request.prologue(), request.headers()))
   205	                    .build());
   206	        }
   207	    }
   208	
   209	    private void handleError(ConnectionContext ctx,
   210	                             RoutingRequest request,
   211	                             RoutingResponse response,
   212	                             Throwable e,
   213	                             ErrorHandler<Throwable> it) {
   214	        // we are only interested in resetting the streams, headers are at the discretion of the error handler
   215	        if (!response.resetStream()) {
   216	            ctx.log(LOGGER,
   217	                    System.Logger.Level.WARNING,
   218	                    "Unable to reset response for error handler, at least part of entity already written. "
   219	                            + "Error handler cannot be invoked.",
   220	                    e);
   221	            throw new CloseConnectionException(
   222	                    "Cannot send response of a simple handler, status and headers already written", e);
   223	        }
   224	        try {
   225	            it.handle(request, response, e);
   226	            response.commit();
   227	            if (!response.isSent()) {
   228	                ctx.log(LOGGER, System.Logger.Level.TRACE, "Exception not handled.", e);
   229	                unhandledError(ctx, request, response, e);
   230	            }
   231	        } catch (HttpException ex) {
   232	            if (ex.getClass().equals(e.getClass())) {
   233	                ctx.log(LOGGER, System.Logger.Level.TRACE, "Failed to handle exception.", ex);
   234	                unhandledError(ctx, request, response, e);
   235	            } else {
   236	                throw ex;
   237	            }
   238	        } catch (Exception ex) {
   239	            ctx.log(LOGGER, System.Logger.Level.TRACE, "Failed to handle exception.", ex);
   240	            unhandledError(ctx, request, response, e);
   241	        }
   242	    }
   243	}

This should be fine because `buffer.length` is the remaining capacity of the target buffer.\n\nBut wait! The `buffer.length = length - writePosition`. Before `write(buffer)`, we wrote `hex.length + 2` bytes (hex, \\r, \\n). So `writePosition = hex.length + 2`. The total capacity is `available + hex.length + 4`. So `buffer.length = available + hex.length + 4 - hex.length - 2 = available + 2`.\n\nBut `toWrite.read(buffer)` would try to read `available + 2` bytes from a buffer that has only `available` bytes. The `read` method returns `Math.min(length, available) = available`. So only `available` bytes are read. Then writePosition advances by `available`. Now writePosition = `hex.length + 2 + available`. \n\nBut wait, `buffer.length` was `available + 2`, but only `available` bytes were read. The remaining 2 bytes of the temporary buffer are unused.         flush();
```java
        closingDelegate.commit();
    } catch (IOException | UncheckedIOException e) {
```

For chunked: the first write is buffered in `firstBuffer` (copied). The second write triggers headers + the combined first and second buffers. But what if there's only one write? Wait, let me re-read. `isChunked` is set in `checkResponseHeaders()`:
```java

        headers.remove(HeaderNames.CONTENT_LENGTH);
        isChunked = true;
        forcedChunked = true;
    } else {
        isChunked = !headers.contains(HeaderNames.CONTENT_LENGTH);
        forcedChunked = headers.contains(HeaderValues.TRANSFER_ENCODING_CHUNKED);
    }
}
```

So `isChunked` is true when there's no content-length or when chunked encoding is forced. 

Now, in `commit()`:
```java

    if (forcedChunked && firstBuffer != null) {
        sendHeadersAndPrepare();
        writeChunked(firstBuffer);
        terminatingChunk(sendTrailers);
    } else {

    }
```

If `isChunked` is true (no content-length) but `firstBuffer == null` (no data was written), it goes to `sendFirstChunkOnly()` which sets content-length to 0. That seems fine.

But if `forcedChunked` is true and `firstBuffer != null`, it writes the chunked response correctly.

Now, the issue about chunked encoding corruption - let me think about what could go wrong.

Wait, I just realized something. The `BufferedOutputStream` wraps `BlockingOutputStream`. When you write to the `BufferedOutputStream`, it buffers data and then flushes to the underlying stream when the buffer is full. But `BufferedOutputStream.write(byte[], int, int)` writes directly if `len >= buffer.length`. Let me check the default buffer size:

From config, `writeBufferSize` defaults to 4096.

So if you write more than 4096 bytes at once, `BufferedOutputStream` bypasses its internal buffer and writes directly to the underlying `BlockingOutputStream`. But if you write less than 4096 bytes, it buffers.

Now, in the `BlockingOutputStream.write(BufferData)`:
- First write: buffer is stored as `firstBuffer` (for chunked optimization)
- Second write: combines first and current buffer, sends headers + both buffers

But the `BufferedOutputStream` might buffer multiple small writes and then flush them as one large write. This could cause issues with the chunked optimization logic!

For example:
1. User writes 1000 bytes → BufferedOutputStream buffers it
2. User writes 1000 bytes → BufferedOutputStream buffers it (now 2000 bytes buffered)
3. User writes 3000 bytes → Now total is 5000 > 4096, BufferedOutputStream flushes: first writes the 4096 buffered bytes, then writes the remaining 904 bytes directly

But wait, that's not how `BufferedOutputStream` works. Let me check:

`BufferedOutputStream.write(byte[], int, int)`:
```java
public synchronized void write(byte b[], int off, int len) throws IOException {
    if (len >= buf.length) {
        /* If the request length exceeds the size of the output buffer,
           flush the output buffer and then write the data directly.
           In this way buffered streams will cascade harmlessly. */
        flushBuffer();
        out.write(b, off, len);
        return;
    }
    if (len > buf.length - count) {
        flushBuffer();
    }
    System.arraycopy(b, off, buf, count, len);
    count += len;
}
```

So if `len >= buf.length` (4096), it flushes the buffer and writes directly. If the buffer would overflow, it flushes first, then copies the new data into the buffer.

Now, the `BlockingOutputStream.write(byte[], int, int)`:
```java
@Override
public void write(byte[] b, int off, int len) throws IOException {
    write(BufferData.create(b, off, len));
}
```

This creates a `FixedBufferData` and calls `write(BufferData)`. 

So, if the application writes 100MB in 524288-byte chunks (as in the PR description), each write is much larger than the 4096 buffer. So `BufferedOutputStream` would flush its buffer (empty) and then call `out.write(b, off, len)` directly, which goes to `BlockingOutputStream.write(byte[], int, int)`.

Now, in `BlockingOutputStream.write(BufferData)`:
- First write: buffer is copied to `firstBuffer` (for chunked optimization)
- But wait! The first write is the only write? No, the application writes multiple chunks.

Let me trace:
1. First `write(524288 bytes)` → `firstBuffer = buffer.copy()` (stores 524288 bytes), returns without writing
2. Second `write(524288 bytes)` → `firstByte` is true, so it sends headers, combines firstBuffer + current buffer, and writes as chunked. Then `firstByte = false`.
3. Subsequent writes: `writeChunked(buffer)` directly.

This looks correct. The chunked encoding should be properly formatted.

But wait, what if there's only ONE write? Then:
- `firstBuffer` has the data
- `commit()` is called
- `firstByte` is true
- If `forcedChunked && firstBuffer != null` → sends headers and writes chunked
- Otherwise → `sendFirstChunkOnly()` which sets content-length (optimization)

If `forcedChunked` is true (chunked was explicitly set by header), it should work correctly. But if chunked is implicit (no content-length set), `forcedChunked` is false, and it would use `sendFirstChunkOnly()` which converts to content-length response. That might be fine actually.

OK, let me think about this differently. Maybe the issue is in the `BufferedOutputStream` interaction. Let me check if there's a race condition or data corruption in the write path.

Actually, let me look at the `writeChunked` method more carefully:

```java
private void writeChunked(BufferData buffer) {
    int available = buffer.available();
    byte[] hex = Integer.toHexString(available).getBytes(StandardCharsets.US_ASCII);

    BufferData toWrite = BufferData.create(available + hex.length + 4);
    toWrite.write(hex);
    toWrite.write('\r');
    toWrite.write('\n');
    toWrite.write(buffer);
    toWrite.write('\r');
    toWrite.write('\n');

    sendListener.data(ctx, toWrite);
    responseBytesTotal += toWrite.available();
    dataWriter.write(toWrite);
}
```

`BufferData.create(available + hex.length + 4)` creates a new `FixedBufferData` with the given size. Then we write hex, \r, \n, the buffer, \r, \n.

But `toWrite.write(buffer)` calls:
```java
public void write(BufferData toWrite) {
    byte[] buffer = new byte[length - writePosition];
    int read = toWrite.read(buffer);
    System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);
    writePosition += read;
}
```

This creates a temporary buffer of size `length - writePosition` which should be `available + hex.length + 4 - (hex.length + 2)` = `available + 2`. Wait, that's `available + 2`, not `available`. But `toWrite.read(buffer)` with `buffer.length = available + 2` would try to read `available + 2` bytes from `toWrite` which only has `available` bytes. But `read` method returns `Math.min(length, available)`, so it would only read `available` bytes. That's fine.

But wait, after `write(hex)` and `write('\r')` and `write('\n')`, the writePosition is `hex.length + 2`. The total capacity is `available + hex.length + 4`. So remaining capacity is `(available + hex.length + 4) - (hex.length + 2)` = `available + 2`. 

Then `write(buffer)` reads `available` bytes from buffer and writes them. WritePosition advances to `hex.length + 2 + available`. Remaining: `(available + hex.length + 4) - (hex.length + 2 + available)` = 2.

Then `write('\r')` and `write('\n')` write the final 2 bytes. Done.

This all looks correct.

Let me check if there's an issue with `BufferData.create(byte[], int, int)` - the method used in `BlockingOutputStream.write(byte[], int, int)`:

```java
@Override
public void write(byte[] b, int off, int len) throws IOException {
    write(BufferData.create(b, off, len));
}
```

`BufferData.create(b, off, len)`:
```java
static BufferData create(byte[] bytes, int position, int length) {
    return new FixedBufferData(bytes, position, length);
}
```

```java
FixedBufferData(byte[] bytes, int position, int length) {
    this.bytes = bytes;
    this.length = length;
    this.writePosition = position + length;
    this.readPosition = position;
}
```

So `readPosition = off` and `writePosition = off + len`. Available = `writePosition - readPosition` = `len`. This is correct.

Now let me check `writeTo` for `FixedBufferData` when used from `NioSocket.write`:

```java
public int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int length) {
    int toWrite = Math.min(writeBuffer.limit() - writeBuffer.position(), writePosition - readPosition);
    toWrite = Math.min(toWrite, length);
    if (toWrite == 0) {
        return 0;
    }
    writeBuffer.put(this.bytes, readPosition, toWrite);
    readPosition += toWrite;
    return toWrite;
}
```

`writeBuffer.limit() - writeBuffer.position()` is the remaining space in the NIO buffer (up to 8192). `writePosition - readPosition` is the available bytes in this buffer. `Math.min(toWrite, length)` further constrains it. Then `writeBuffer.put(this.bytes, readPosition, toWrite)` copies the bytes. This looks correct.

Wait, I think I need to look at the `NioSocket.write` method again:

```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
            writeBuffer.clear();
            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
            writeBuffer.flip();
            delegate.write(writeBuffer);
        }
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

For a large buffer (e.g., 100MB), `buffer.available()` returns 100M. But `writeBuffer` is only 8192 bytes. So `buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available())` writes at most 8192 bytes. Then `delegate.write(writeBuffer)` writes those 8192 bytes to the socket. Then the loop continues until `buffer.consumed()` is true.

But wait, for a `FixedBufferData`, the `writeTo` method modifies `readPosition`. So subsequent iterations will continue from where we left off. This is correct.


This means the client received a chunk size line that doesn't end with CR (`\r`). The chunk format is:
```
<chunk-size-in-hex>\r\n
<chunk-data>\r\n
```

If the `\r` after the chunk size is missing, the client would see something like `<hex-digits>\n` instead of `<hex-digits>\r\n`. Or maybe the `\r` after the chunk data is missing.

What could cause this? If the `writeChunked` method writes incorrect data, or if the data gets corrupted during write.

Let me think about what could cause this:
1. If the `\r\n` after chunk data is missing, the client would read part of the next chunk's header as part of the previous chunk's data
2. If the `\r\n` after chunk size is missing, the client would read data bytes as part of the hex size

Both would cause "Malformed encoding" errors.

For a `CompositeBufferData`, `toWrite.read(buffer)` calls `CompositeListBufferData.read(byte[], int, int)`:
```java
public int read(byte[] buffer, int position, int length) {
    int myPosition = position;
    int remaining = length;

    for (BufferData datum : data) {
        if (datum.available() > 0) {
            int read = datum.read(buffer, myPosition, remaining);
            myPosition += read;
            remaining -= read;
            if (remaining == 0) {
                break;
            }
        }
    }

    return myPosition - position;
}
```

This reads up to `length` bytes from the composite buffer. This should be fine because `buffer.length` is the remaining capacity of the target buffer.

But wait! The `buffer.length = length - writePosition`. Before `write(buffer)`, we wrote `hex.length + 2` bytes (hex, \r, \n). So `writePosition = hex.length + 2`. The total capacity is `available + hex.length + 4`. So `buffer.length = available + hex.length + 4 - hex.length - 2 = available + 2`.

But `toWrite.read(buffer)` would try to read `available + 2` bytes from a buffer that has only `available` bytes. The `read` method returns `Math.min(length, available) = available`. So only `available` bytes are read. Then writePosition advances by `available`. Now writePosition = `hex.length + 2 + available`. 

But wait, `buffer.length` was `available + 2`, but only `available` bytes were read. The remaining 2 bytes of the temporary buffer are unused. This is fine.

After that, we write `\r` and `\n` which consume the last 2 bytes. So the total is exactly the capacity.

This all looks correct. I'm not finding the bug yet.

Let me look at the other side: the `sendFirstChunkOnly()` method. If the response doesn't have forced chunked encoding and there's only one buffer, it uses content-length:

```java
private void sendFirstChunkOnly() {
    int contentLength;
    if (firstBuffer == null) {
        headers.set(HeaderValues.CONTENT_LENGTH_ZERO);
        contentLength = 0;
    } else {
        headers.set(HeaderValues.create(HeaderNames.CONTENT_LENGTH, String.valueOf(firstBuffer.available())));
        contentLength = firstBuffer.available();
    }
    isChunked = false;
    headers.remove(HeaderNames.TRANSFER_ENCODING);

    // at this moment, we must send headers
    Status usedStatus = status.get();
    sendListener.status(ctx, usedStatus);
    sendListener.headers(ctx, headers);
    BufferData bufferData = BufferData.growing(contentLength + 256);
    nonEntityBytes(headers, usedStatus, bufferData, keepAlive, validateHeaders);

    if (firstBuffer != null) {
        bufferData.write(firstBuffer);
    }

    sendListener.data(ctx, bufferData);
    responseBytesTotal += bufferData.available();
    dataWriter.write(bufferData);
}
```

This creates a `GrowingBufferData` and writes headers and body. `GrowingBufferData` should handle writes correctly.

    27	class GrowingBufferData implements BufferData {
    28	    private byte[] bytes;
    29	    private int length;
    30	    private int writePosition;
    31	    private int readPosition;
    32	
    33	    GrowingBufferData(int initialLength) {
    34	        int usedInitial = Math.max(initialLength, 256);
    35	        this.bytes = new byte[usedInitial];
    36	        this.length = 0;
    37	    }
    38	
    39	    public boolean ready() {
    40	        return writePosition > readPosition;
    41	    }
    42	
    43	    @Override
    44	    public GrowingBufferData reset() {
    45	        this.writePosition = 0;
    46	        this.readPosition = 0;
    47	        return this;
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    @Override
    51	    public BufferData rewind() {
    52	        this.readPosition = 0;
    53	        return this;
    54	    }
    55	
    56	    @Override
    57	    public BufferData clear() {
    58	        reset();
    59	        length = 0;
    60	        return this;
    61	    }
    62	
    63	    @Override
    64	    public void writeTo(OutputStream out) {
    65	        try {
    66	            out.write(bytes, readPosition, writePosition - readPosition);
    67	            readPosition = writePosition;
    68	        } catch (IOException e) {
    69	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    70	        }
    71	    }
    72	
    73	    @Override
    74	    public int readFrom(InputStream in) {
    75	        try {
    76	            int read = in.read(bytes, writePosition, bytes.length - writePosition);
    77	            if (read > 0) {
    78	                writePosition += read;
    79	            }
    80	            return read;
    81	        } catch (IOException e) {
    82	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    83	        }
    84	    }
    85	
    86	    @Override
    87	    public int readFrom(ByteBuffer buf) {
    88	        int read = Math.min(buf.remaining(), bytes.length - writePosition);
    89	        buf.get(bytes, writePosition, read);
    90	        writePosition += read;
    91	        return read;
    92	    }
    93	
    94	    @Override
    95	    public int read() {
    96	        if (readPosition >= writePosition) {
    97	            throw new ArrayIndexOutOfBoundsException("This buffer has " + length
    98	                                                             + " bytes, requested to read at " + readPosition);
    99	        }
   100	        return bytes[readPosition++] & 0xFF;
   101	    }
   102	
   103	    public int read(byte[] bytes, int position, int length) {
   104	        int available = writePosition - readPosition;
   105	        int toRead = Math.min(length, available);
   106	
   107	        System.arraycopy(this.bytes, readPosition, bytes, position, toRead);
   108	
   109	        readPosition += toRead;
   110	        return toRead;
   111	    }
   112	
   113	    @Override
   114	    public String readString(int length, Charset charset) {
   115	        String result = new String(bytes, readPosition, length, charset);
   116	        readPosition += length;
   117	        return result;
   118	    }
   119	
   120	    public boolean consumed() {
   121	        return readPosition == writePosition;
   122	    }
   123	
   124	    public GrowingBufferData write(int value) {
   125	        ensureSize(1);
   126	        this.bytes[writePosition++] = (byte) value;
   127	        this.length = Math.max(length, writePosition);
   128	        return this;
   129	    }
   130	
   131	    @Override
   132	    public int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int limit) {
   133	        int toWrite = Math.min(writeBuffer.limit() - writeBuffer.position(), writePosition - readPosition);
   134	        toWrite = Math.min(toWrite, limit);
   135	        if (toWrite == 0) {
   136	            return 0;
   137	        }
   138	        writeBuffer.put(this.bytes, readPosition, toWrite);
   139	        readPosition += toWrite;
   140	        return toWrite;
   141	    }
   142	
   143	    @Override
   144	    public void write(byte[] bytes, int offset, int length) {
   145	        ensureSize(length);
   146	        System.arraycopy(bytes, offset, this.bytes, writePosition, length);
   147	        writePosition += length;
   148	        this.length = Math.max(this.length, writePosition);
   149	    }
   150	
   151	    @Override
   152	    public void write(BufferData toWrite) {
   153	        ensureSize(toWrite.available());
   154	        byte[] buffer = new byte[toWrite.available()];
   155	        int read = toWrite.read(buffer);
   156	        System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);
   157	        writePosition += read;
   158	    }
   159	
   160	    @Override
   161	    public void write(BufferData toWrite, int length) {
   162	        ensureSize(length);
   163	        byte[] buffer = new byte[length];
   164	        int read = toWrite.read(buffer);
   165	        System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);
   166	        writePosition += read;
   167	    }
   168	
   169	    @Override
   170	    public String debugDataBinary() {
   171	        return BufferUtil.debugDataBinary(bytes, 0, writePosition);
   172	    }
   173	
   174	    @Override
   175	    public String debugDataHex(boolean fullBuffer) {
   176	        return BufferUtil.debugDataHex(bytes, fullBuffer ? 0 : readPosition, writePosition);
   177	    }
   178	
   179	    @Override
   180	    public int available() {
   181	        return writePosition - readPosition;
   182	    }
   183	
   184	    @Override
   185	    public void skip(int length) {
   186	        readPosition += length;
   187	    }
   188	
   189	    @Override
   190	    public int indexOf(byte aByte) {
   191	        for (int i = readPosition; i < (readPosition + available()); i++) {
   192	            if (bytes[i] == aByte) {
   193	                return i - readPosition;
   194	            }
   195	        }
   196	        return -1;
   197	    }
   198	
   199	    @Override
   200	    public int lastIndexOf(byte aByte, int length) {
   201	        for (int i = length - 1; i >= readPosition; i--) {
   202	            byte b = bytes[i];
   203	            if (b == aByte) {
   204	                return i - readPosition;
   205	            }
   206	        }
   207	        return -1;
   208	    }
   209	
   210	    @Override
   211	    public BufferData trim(int x) {
   212	        if (available() < x) {
   213	            throw new IllegalArgumentException("Trimming more bytes than available");
   214	        }
   215	        writePosition -= x;
   216	        length -= x;
   217	        return this;
   218	    }
   219	
   220	    @Override
   221	    public int capacity() {
   222	        return length - writePosition;
   223	    }
   224	
   225	    @Override
   226	    public int get(int index) {
   227	        return bytes[readPosition + index];
   228	    }
   229	
   230	    @Override
   231	    public String toString() {
   232	        return "grow: l=" + length + ", r=" + readPosition + ", w=" + writePosition + ", c=" + bytes.length;
   233	    }
   234	
   235	    byte[] bytes() {
   236	        return Arrays.copyOfRange(bytes, 0, length);
   237	    }
   238	
   239	    private void ensureSize(int i) {
   240	        if (this.bytes.length > writePosition + i) {
   241	            return;
   242	        }
   243	
   244	        byte[] current = this.bytes;
   245	        int currentLength = current.length;
   246	        int newLength = currentLength * 2;
   247	        newLength = Math.max(newLength, writePosition + i);
   248	        if (newLength < currentLength) {
   249	            // int overflow
   250	            throw new IllegalStateException("Growing buffer too big, cannot increase size");
   251	        }
   252	        this.bytes = new byte[newLength];
   253	        System.arraycopy(current, 0, this.bytes, 0, length);
   254	    }
   255	}

Now let me look at the `CompositeListBufferData` more carefully. Specifically, look at the `writeTo` method versus the `CompositeArrayBufferData.writeTo`:

Both are identical. But I notice something: in `CompositeListBufferData`:

```java
public int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int limit) {
    int written = 0;

    for (BufferData datum : data) {
        if (datum.consumed()) {
            continue;
        }
        int datumWrote = datum.writeTo(writeBuffer, limit - written);
        if (datumWrote == 0) {
            // not consumed and wrote 0 -> full
            break;
        }
        written += datumWrote;
    }

    return written;
}
```

If `datumWrote == 0` and the datum is not consumed, it breaks out of the loop. This means if a single datum can't be written (because writeBuffer is full), it stops. But the outer loop in `NioSocket.write` will call again after writing to the socket. So this should be fine.

Let me now focus on a different area. The PR mentions the issue started in 4.4.0. Maybe the issue is in the `writeChunked` method that combines the first and second buffer:

```java
if (firstByte) {
    ...
    sendHeadersAndPrepare();
    firstByte = false;
    BufferData combined = BufferData.create(firstBuffer, buffer);
    writeChunked(combined);
    firstBuffer = null;
}
```

`BufferData.create(firstBuffer, buffer)` creates a `CompositeArrayBufferData` with two buffers. Then `writeChunked(combined)` calls:

```java
int available = combined.available();  // sum of both buffers
byte[] hex = Integer.toHexString(available).getBytes(StandardCharsets.US_ASCII);

BufferData toWrite = BufferData.create(available + hex.length + 4);
toWrite.write(hex);
toWrite.write('\r');
toWrite.write('\n');
toWrite.write(combined);   // writes the composite buffer
toWrite.write('\r');
toWrite.write('\n');
```

Now, `toWrite.write(combined)` calls `FixedBufferData.write(BufferData)`:
```java
public void write(BufferData toWrite) {
    byte[] buffer = new byte[length - writePosition];
    int read = toWrite.read(buffer);
    System.arraycopy(buffer, 0, this.bytes, writePosition, read);
    writePosition += read;
}
```

For a `CompositeArrayBufferData`, `read(buffer)` calls:
```java
public int read(byte[] buffer, int position, int length) {
    int myPosition = position;
    int remaining = length;

    for (BufferData datum : data) {
        if (datum.available() > 0) {
            int read = datum.read(buffer, myPosition, remaining);
            myPosition += read;
            remaining -= read;
            if (remaining == 0) {
                break;
            }
        }
    }

    return myPosition - position;
}
```

This reads from each sub-buffer until `remaining == 0` or all sub-buffers are exhausted. For a `FixedBufferData`, `read(byte[], int, int)` is:
```java
public int read(byte[] bytes, int position, int length) {
    int available = this.writePosition - readPosition;
    int toRead = Math.min(length, available);
    System.arraycopy(this.bytes, readPosition, bytes, position, toRead);
    readPosition += toRead;
    return toRead;
}
```

This should correctly read all available bytes from each sub-buffer. But wait, after reading, the sub-buffer's `readPosition` advances. So if we later call `available()` on the composite, it would be 0 (since we consumed all sub-buffers). But `toWrite.write(combined)` reads all bytes at once, so this should be fine.

    24	import io.helidon.http.Status;
    25	import io.helidon.webclient.http1.Http1Client;
    26	import io.helidon.webclient.http1.Http1ClientResponse;
    27	import io.helidon.webserver.http.HttpRouting;
    28	import io.helidon.webserver.http.ServerRequest;
    29	import io.helidon.webserver.http.ServerResponse;
    30	import io.helidon.webserver.testing.junit5.ServerTest;
    31	import io.helidon.webserver.testing.junit5.SetUpRoute;
    32	
    33	import org.junit.jupiter.api.Test;
    34	
    35	import static io.helidon.http.Method.GET;
    36	import static org.hamcrest.CoreMatchers.is;
    37	import static org.hamcrest.MatcherAssert.assertThat;
    38	
    39	@ServerTest
    40	class OutputStreamTest {
    41	
    42	    private final Http1Client client;
    43	
    44	    OutputStreamTest(Http1Client client) {
    45	        this.client = client;
    46	    }
    47	
    48	    @SetUpRoute
    49	    static void routing(HttpRouting.Builder router) {
    50	        router.route(GET, "/outputStream", Service::outputStream);
    51	    }
    52	
    53	    @Test
    54	    void verifyAutoFlush() {
    55	        try (Http1ClientResponse response = client.get("/outputStream").request()) {
    56	            assertThat(response.status(), is(Status.OK_200));
    57	            String entity = response.entity().as(String.class);
    58	            assertThat(entity, is("Hello World"));
    59	        }
    60	    }
    61	
    62	    protected static class Service {
    63	
    64	        public static void outputStream(ServerRequest req, ServerResponse res) throws IOException {
    65	            InputStream in = new ByteArrayInputStream("Hello World".getBytes(StandardCharsets.UTF_8));
    66	            in.transferTo(res.outputStream());      // no explicit flush
    67	        }
    68	    }
    69	}

    17	package io.helidon.webserver.tests;
    18	
    19	import io.helidon.common.testing.http.junit5.SocketHttpClient;
    20	import io.helidon.http.ClientResponseHeaders;
    21	import io.helidon.http.Header;
    22	import io.helidon.http.HeaderNames;
    23	import io.helidon.http.HeaderValues;
    24	import io.helidon.http.Method;
    25	import io.helidon.webserver.http.HttpRules;
    26	import io.helidon.webserver.testing.junit5.ServerTest;
    27	import io.helidon.webserver.testing.junit5.SetUpRoute;
    28	
    29	import org.junit.jupiter.api.Test;
    30	
    31	import static io.helidon.common.testing.http.junit5.HttpHeaderMatcher.hasHeader;
    32	import static org.hamcrest.CoreMatchers.containsString;
    33	import static org.hamcrest.CoreMatchers.is;
    34	import static org.hamcrest.CoreMatchers.notNullValue;
    35	import static org.hamcrest.CoreMatchers.startsWith;
    36	import static org.hamcrest.MatcherAssert.assertThat;
    37	
    38	/**
    39	 * Tests transfer encoding.
    40	 */
    41	@ServerTest
    42	class TransferEncodingTest {
    43	    private static final Header CONTENT_LENGTH_NINE = HeaderValues.create(HeaderNames.CONTENT_LENGTH, "9");
    44	    private final SocketHttpClient socketHttpClient;
    45	
    46	    TransferEncodingTest(SocketHttpClient socketHttpClient) {
    47	        this.socketHttpClient = socketHttpClient;
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    @SetUpRoute
    51	    static void routing(HttpRules rules) {
    52	        rules.get("/length", (req, res) -> {
    53	                    String payload = "It works!";
    54	                    res.contentLength(payload.length());
    55	                    res.send(payload);
    56	                })
    57	                .get("/chunked", (req, res) -> {
    58	                    String payload = "It works!";
    59	                    res.headers().add(HeaderValues.TRANSFER_ENCODING_CHUNKED);
    60	                    res.send(payload);
    61	                })
    62	                .get("/optimized", (req, res) -> {
    63	                    String payload = "It works!";
    64	                    res.send(payload);
    65	                })
    66	                .get("/empty", (req, res) -> {
    67	                    res.send();
    68	                })
    69	                .get("/emptychunked", (req, res) -> {
    70	                    res.headers().add(HeaderValues.TRANSFER_ENCODING_CHUNKED);
    71	                    res.send();
    72	                });
    73	    }
    74	
    75	    /**
    76	     * Test content length when no payload in response.
    77	     */
    78	    @Test
    79	    void testEmptyContentLength() {
    80	        String s = socketHttpClient.sendAndReceive(Method.GET, "/empty", null);
    81	
    82	        ClientResponseHeaders headers = SocketHttpClient.headersFromResponse(s);
    83	        assertThat(headers, hasHeader(HeaderValues.CONTENT_LENGTH_ZERO));
    84	    }
    85	
    86	    /**
    87	     * Test when no payload in response but response was forced to chunked.
    88	     */
    89	    @Test
    90	    void testEmptyChunked() {
    91	        String s = socketHttpClient.sendAndReceive(Method.GET, "/emptychunked", null);
    92	        ClientResponseHeaders headers = SocketHttpClient.headersFromResponse(s);
    93	        assertThat(headers, hasHeader(HeaderValues.TRANSFER_ENCODING_CHUNKED));
    94	    }
    95	
    96	    /**
    97	     * Test content length
    98	     */
    99	    @Test
   100	    void testContentLength() {
   101	        String s = socketHttpClient.sendAndReceive(Method.GET, "/length", null);
   102	        assertThat(cutPayloadAndCheckHeadersFormat(s), is("It works!"));
   103	        ClientResponseHeaders headers = SocketHttpClient.headersFromResponse(s);
   104	        assertThat(headers, hasHeader(CONTENT_LENGTH_NINE));
   105	    }
   106	
   107	    /**
   108	     * Test chunked encoding.
   109	     */
   110	    @Test
   111	    void testChunkedEncoding() {
   112	        String s = socketHttpClient.sendAndReceive(Method.GET, "/chunked", null);
   113	        assertThat(cutPayloadAndCheckHeadersFormat(s), is("9\nIt works!\n0\n\n"));
   114	        ClientResponseHeaders headers = SocketHttpClient.headersFromResponse(s);
   115	        assertThat(headers, hasHeader(HeaderValues.TRANSFER_ENCODING_CHUNKED));
   116	    }
   117	
   118	    /**
   119	     * Test optimized or content length in this case.
   120	     */
   121	    @Test
   122	    void testOptimized() {
   123	        String s = socketHttpClient.sendAndReceive(Method.GET, "/optimized", null);
   124	        assertThat(cutPayloadAndCheckHeadersFormat(s), is("It works!"));
   125	        ClientResponseHeaders headers = SocketHttpClient.headersFromResponse(s);
   126	        assertThat(headers, hasHeader(CONTENT_LENGTH_NINE));
   127	    }
   128	
   129	    private String cutPayloadAndCheckHeadersFormat(String response) {
   130	        assertThat(response, notNullValue());
   131	        int index = response.indexOf("\n\n");
   132	        if (index < 0) {
   133	            throw new AssertionError("Missing end of headers in response!");
   134	        }
   135	        String headers = response.substring(0, index);
   136	        String[] lines = headers.split("\\n");
   137	        assertThat(lines[0], startsWith("HTTP/"));
   138	        for (int i = 1; i < lines.length; i++) {
   139	            assertThat(lines[i], containsString(":"));
   140	        }
   141	        return response.substring(index + 2);
   142	    }
   143	}

This would cause an infinite loop.\n\nCan `writeTo` return 0 when `buffer` is not consumed? Let me check `FixedBufferData.writeTo`:\n\n```java\npublic int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int length) {\n    int toWrite = Math.min(writeBuffer.limit() - writeBuffer.position(), writePosition - readPosition);\n    toWrite = Math.min(toWrite, length);\n    if (toWrite == 0) {\n        return 0;\n    }\n    writeBuffer.put(this.bytes, readPosition, toWrite);\n    readPosition += toWrite;\n    return toWrite;\n}\n```\n\nIf `writeBuffer.limit() - writeBuffer.position()` is 0 (i.e., writeBuffer is full), and the buffer still has bytes, `toWrite` would be 0. Then it returns 0. But this should only happen if `writeBuffer` is already full. Unless the capacity is 0, which it\'s not (it\'s 8192). Let me check if the second report uses a custom configuration.\n\nActually, let me focus on the `SmartSocketWriter` issue I identified earlier. The race condition between the async writer thread and the main thread when switching from async to sync mode could cause data corruption.\n\nLet me look at this more carefully:\n\n```java\npublic class SmartSocketWriter extends SocketWriter {\n    private static final long WINDOW_SIZE = 1000;\n    private static final double QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD = 2.0;\n\n    private final SocketWriterAsync asyncWriter;\n    private volatile long windowIndex;\n    private volatile boolean asyncMode;\n\n    SmartSocketWriter(ExecutorService executor, HelidonSocket socket, int writeQueueLength) {\n        super(socket);\n        this.asyncWriter = new SocketWriterAsync(executor, socket, writeQueueLength);\n        this.asyncMode = true;\n        this.windowIndex = 0L;\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void write(BufferData... buffers) {\n        for (BufferData buffer : buffers) {\n            write(buffer);\n        }\n    }\n\n    @Override\n    public void write(BufferData buffer) {\n        if (asyncMode) {\n            asyncWriter.write(buffer);\n            if (++windowIndex % WINDOW_SIZE == 0 && asyncWriter.avgQueueSize() < QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD) {\n                asyncMode = false;\n            }\n        } else {\n            asyncWriter.drainQueue();\n            writeNow(buffer);       // blocking write\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nThe problem: when switching from async to sync mode (`asyncMode = false`), the async thread might still be writing. The `drainQueue()` drains remaining buffers from the queue, but the async thread might have already taken a buffer and is writing it. Then `writeNow(buffer)` writes concurrently with the async thread\'s write.\n\nBut wait, there\'s another issue. Even without the race, the transition from async to sync is not safe. Let me trace through a scenario:\n\n1. Thread A (HTTP handler): calls `write(buffer1)` → asyncMode=true → `asyncWriter.write(buffer1)` puts buffer1 in queue\n2. Thread B (async writer): takes buffer1, starts writing via `writeNow(composite(buffer1))`\n3. Thread A: calls `write(buffer2)` → asyncMode=true → `asyncWriter.write(buffer2)` puts buffer2 in queue\n4. ... (998 more writes)\n5. Thread A: calls `write(buffer1000)` → `windowIndex` hits 1000, `avgQueueSize` < 2.0, `asyncMode = false`\n6. Thread A: calls `write(buffer1001)` → asyncMode=false → `asyncWriter.drainQueue()` → polls any remaining buffers and writes them\n7. Thread A: calls `writeNow(buffer1001)` → writes directly\n\nBut what about Thread B? It might be in step 2, still writing buffer1. Or it might have finished buffer1 and be blocked on `writeQueue.take()` waiting for more. If Thread B is blocked on `take()`, then `drainQueue()` in step 6 will drain everything, and Thread B will stay blocked. Then Thread A writes directly in step 7. This is safe.\n\nBut if Thread B is still writing buffer1 when Thread A does steps 6-7, then both threads are writing to the socket concurrently! This is the race condition.\n\nHowever, for this race to cause the symptoms described (missing CR, malformed chunked encoding), the concurrent writes would need to interleave the data. Since `NioSocket.write` uses a shared `writeBuffer`, concurrent writes would corrupt the data.\n\nBut this only affects the `SmartSocketWriter`, which is not the default. Let me check if there\'s a simpler bug that affects the default path.\n\nActually, let me look at the `SocketWriterAsync` more carefully. Let me look at the code more carefully to find potential bugs.\n\nLet me look at the `Http1ServerResponse.outputStream()` method:\n\n```java\n@Override\npublic OutputStream outputStream() {\n    beforeSend();\n    return outputStream(false);\n}\n```\n\nAnd `outputStream(boolean)`:\n```java\nprivate OutputStream outputStream(boolean skipEncoders) {\n    if (isSent) {\n        throw new IllegalStateException("Response already sent");\n    }\n    if (streamingEntity) {\n        throw new IllegalStateException("OutputStream already obtained");\n    }\n    streamingEntity = true;\n\n    BlockingOutputStream bos = new BlockingOutputStream(...);\n    int writeBufferSize = ctx.listenerContext().config().writeBufferSize();\n    outputStream = new ClosingBufferedOutputStream(bos, writeBufferSize);\n\n    OutputStream encodedOutputStream = outputStream;\n    if (!skipEncoders) {\n        encodedOutputStream = contentEncode(outputStream);\n        bos.checkResponseHeaders();     // headers can be augmented by encoders\n    }\n    return outputStreamFilter == null ? encodedOutputStream : outputStreamFilter.apply(encodedOutputStream);\n}\n```\n\nThe `bos.checkResponseHeaders()` is called after `contentEncode()`. The `contentEncode()` method may add headers (like `Content-Encoding`). Then `checkResponseHeaders()` determines if chunked encoding should be used.\n\nNow, look at `send(byte[], int, int)`:\n```java\n@Override\npublic void send(byte[] bytes, int position, int length) {\n    if (isNoEntityStatus && length > 0) {\n        status(noEntityInternalError(status()));\n        return;\n    }\n\n    beforeSend();\n\n    if (outputStreamFilter == null && !headers.contains(HeaderNames.TRAILER)) {\n        byte[] entity = entityBytes(bytes, position, length);\n        BufferData bufferData = (bytes != entity) ? responseBuffer(entity)\n                : responseBuffer(entity, position, length);\n        bytesWritten = bufferData.available();\n        isSent = true;\n        request.reset();\n        dataWriter.write(bufferData);\n        afterSend();\n    } else {\n        boolean skipEncoders = (length == 0);\n        try (OutputStream os = outputStream(skipEncoders)) {\n            os.write(bytes, position, length);\n        } catch (IOException e) {\n            throw new ServerConnectionException("Failed to write response", e);\n        }\n    }\n}\n```\n\nWhen `outputStreamFilter != null` or trailers are present, it uses `outputStream()` and closes it. The close triggers `ClosingBufferedOutputStream.close()` which sets `closing = true` and flushes. But then `commit()` is never called! Wait, it\'s called later by the routing framework. Let me check...\n\nIn `HttpRoutingImpl.RoutingExecutor.call()`:\n```java\nif (result == RoutingResult.FINISH) {\n    response.commit();\n    return null;\n}\n```\n\nSo `commit()` is always called after the handler returns. Then `commit()` is called, which calls `outputStream.commit()` → `ClosingBufferedOutputStream.commit()` → flush + `BlockingOutputStream.commit()`.\n\nBut `BlockingOutputStream.commit()` has:\n```java\nif (firstByte) {\n    if (forcedChunked && firstBuffer != null) {\n        sendHeadersAndPrepare();\n        writeChunked(firstBuffer);\n        terminatingChunk(sendTrailers);\n    } else {\n        sendFirstChunkOnly();\n    }\n} else if (isChunked) {\n    terminatingChunk(sendTrailers);\n}\n```\n\nThe data has already been written to the socket via `dataWriter.write()`. But `commit()` may also write the terminating chunk for chunked responses, or may do nothing for content-length responses.\n\nWait, I think I found a bug! Let me look at the flow for `send()` with `outputStreamFilter != null`:\n\n1. `send()` calls `outputStream(skipEncoders)` which creates a new `BlockingOutputStream` and `ClosingBufferedOutputStream`\n2. `os.write(bytes, position, length)` writes data\n3. `os.close()` → `ClosingBufferedOutputStream.close()` → `closingDelegate.closing()` + `delegate.close()`\n4. `delegate.close()` → `BufferedOutputStream.close()` → flush + close\n5. `BlockingOutputStream` receives the write. Let me think about this from a completely different angle. Maybe the issue is in the `NioSocket.write` method and its handling of the ByteBuffer.

```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
            writeBuffer.clear();
            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
            writeBuffer.flip();
            delegate.write(writeBuffer);
        }
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

The `writeBuffer` is reused. `clear()` sets position=0, limit=capacity. `buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available())` writes up to `writeBuffer` capacity bytes. `flip()` sets limit=position, position=0. `delegate.write(writeBuffer)` writes the data to the socket.

But wait, what if `buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available())` returns 0? Then `writeBuffer.flip()` sets limit=0, and `delegate.write(writeBuffer)` writes 0 bytes. But `buffer` is not consumed, so the loop continues indefinitely! This would cause an infinite loop.

Can `writeTo` return 0 when `buffer` is not consumed? Let me check `FixedBufferData.writeTo`:

```java
public int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int length) {
    int toWrite = Math.min(writeBuffer.limit() - writeBuffer.position(), writePosition - readPosition);
    toWrite = Math.min(toWrite, length);
    if (toWrite == 0) {
        return 0;
    }
    writeBuffer.put(this.bytes, readPosition, toWrite);
    readPosition += toWrite;
    return toWrite;
}
```

If `writeBuffer.limit() - writeBuffer.position()` is 0 (i.e., writeBuffer is full), and the buffer still has bytes, `toWrite` would be 0. Then it returns 0. But this should only happen if `writeBuffer` is already full. But we just called `clear()` on it, so it should be empty.

Wait, `clear()` on a ByteBuffer sets position=0 and limit=capacity. So `limit - position = capacity`. Unless the capacity is 0, which it's not (it's 8192). So `toWrite` should never be 0 when the buffer has bytes.

But what about `CompositeListBufferData.writeTo`?

```java
public int writeTo(ByteBuffer writeBuffer, int limit) {
    int written = 0;
    for (BufferData datum : data) {
        if (datum.consumed()) {
            continue;
        }
        int datumWrote = datum.writeTo(writeBuffer, limit - written);
        if (datumWrote == 0) {
            // not consumed and wrote 0 -> full
            break;
        }
        written += datumWrote;
    }
    return written;
}
```

If a datum is not consumed but `datum.writeTo` returns 0, it breaks. But if no bytes were written at all (`written == 0`) and the buffer is not consumed, the loop in `NioSocket.write` will try again. But the writeBuffer is full? No, we just cleared it. So the datum's `writeTo` should not return 0.
