Actually, let me focus on the `SmartSocketWriter` issue I identified earlier. The race condition between the async writer thread and the main thread when switching from async to sync mode could cause data corruption.

Let me look at this more carefully:

```java
public class SmartSocketWriter extends SocketWriter {
    private static final long WINDOW_SIZE = 1000;
    private static final double QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD = 2.0;

    private final SocketWriterAsync asyncWriter;
    private volatile long windowIndex;
    private volatile boolean asyncMode;

    SmartSocketWriter(ExecutorService executor, HelidonSocket socket, int writeQueueLength) {
        super(socket);
        this.asyncWriter = new SocketWriterAsync(executor, socket, writeQueueLength);
        this.asyncMode = true;
        this.windowIndex = 0L;
    }

    @Override
    public void write(BufferData... buffers) {
        for (BufferData buffer : buffers) {
            write(buffer);
        }
    }

    @Override
    public void write(BufferData buffer) {
        if (asyncMode) {
            asyncWriter.write(buffer);
            if (++windowIndex % WINDOW_SIZE == 0 && asyncWriter.avgQueueSize() < QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD) {
                asyncMode = false;
            }
        } else {
            asyncWriter.drainQueue();
            writeNow(buffer);       // blocking write
        }
    }
}
```

The problem: when switching from async to sync mode (`asyncMode = false`), the async thread might still be writing. The `drainQueue()` drains remaining buffers from the queue, but the async thread might have already taken a buffer and is writing it. Then `writeNow(buffer)` writes concurrently with the async thread's write.

But wait, there's another issue. Even without the race, the transition from async to sync is not safe. Let me trace through a scenario:

1. Thread A (HTTP handler): calls `write(buffer1)` → asyncMode=true → `asyncWriter.write(buffer1)` puts buffer1 in queue
2. Thread B (async writer): takes buffer1, starts writing via `writeNow(composite(buffer1))`
3. Thread A: calls `write(buffer2)` → asyncMode=true → `asyncWriter.write(buffer2)` puts buffer2 in queue
4. ... (998 more writes)
5. Thread A: calls `write(buffer1000)` → `windowIndex` hits 1000, `avgQueueSize` < 2.0, `asyncMode = false`
6. Thread A: calls `write(buffer1001)` → asyncMode=false → `asyncWriter.drainQueue()` → polls any remaining buffers and writes them
7. Thread A: calls `writeNow(buffer1001)` → writes directly

But what about Thread B? It might be in step 2, still writing buffer1. Or it might have finished buffer1 and be blocked on `writeQueue.take()` waiting for more. If Thread B is blocked on `take()`, then `drainQueue()` in step 6 will drain everything, and Thread B will stay blocked. Then Thread A writes directly in step 7. This is safe.

But if Thread B is still writing buffer1 when Thread A does steps 6-7, then both threads are writing to the socket concurrently! This is the race condition.

However, for this race to cause the symptoms described (missing CR, malformed chunked encoding), the concurrent writes would need to interleave the data. Since `NioSocket.write` uses a shared `writeBuffer`, concurrent writes would corrupt the data.

But this only affects the `SmartSocketWriter`, which is not the default. Let me check if there's a simpler bug that affects the default path.

Actually, let me look at the `SocketWriterAsync` more carefully. There's a potential issue with the `write` method:

```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    checkRunning();
    try {
        if (!writeQueue.offer(buffer, 10, TimeUnit.SECONDS)) {
            checkRunning();
            throw new IllegalStateException("Failed to write data to queue, timed out");
        }
    } catch (InterruptedException e) {
        throw new IllegalStateException("Interrupted while trying to write to a queue", e);
    }
}
```

If the queue is full, it blocks for up to 10 seconds. If it times out, it throws an exception. But the queue size is `writeQueueLength` which defaults to... wait, `writeQueueLength` defaults to 0, so `SocketWriterDirect` is used, not `SocketWriterAsync`. 

OK, so the async writers are not used by default. Let me look at this from yet another angle.

Let me re-read the PR description:
> "If using chunked transfer, I occasionally see 'missing CR' or 'Malformed encoding found in chunked-encoding' or something similar depending on client."
> "If sending content-length header, the transfer occasionally just gets stuck completely."

"Gets stuck completely" - this sounds like a deadlock or infinite loop. Let me check if there's any place where the code could hang.

Looking at `NioSocket.write`:
```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
            writeBuffer.clear();
            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
            writeBuffer.flip();
            delegate.write(writeBuffer);
        }
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

If `buffer.writeTo` returns 0 and the buffer is not consumed, this would loop forever. But as I analyzed, `writeTo` should not return 0 if the buffer has bytes and the writeBuffer was just cleared.

But wait! What if `buffer` is a `CompositeBufferData` and one of its sub-buffers has 0 available bytes? Let's check:

`CompositeListBufferData.writeTo` iterates through data items. If a datum is consumed, it's skipped. If a datum is not consumed but `datum.writeTo` returns 0, it breaks. If ALL data are consumed, it returns whatever was written (which could be 0 if all data were already consumed). 

But in the loop, `while (!buffer.consumed())` would exit if all data were consumed. So if a composite buffer has all its data already consumed, it would exit.

But what if there's a bug where `consumed()` returns false but `writeTo` returns 0? Let me check...

For `CompositeListBufferData`:
```java
public boolean consumed() {
    boolean consumed = true;
    for (BufferData datum : data) {
        if (!datum.consumed()) {
            consumed = false;
        }
    }
    return consumed;
}
```

If any datum is not consumed, it returns false. But `writeTo` might skip all non-consumed data if they all return 0. That would be a bug in the sub-buffer's `writeTo`.

But I don't see how a `FixedBufferData` or `ReadOnlyArrayData` could have `consumed() == false` and `writeTo` return 0 (unless the writeBuffer is full, which it shouldn't be after `clear()`).

OK let me try yet another approach. Let me look at the `BufferData` implementations for any threading issues. The `NioSocket.writeBuffer` is not thread-safe - but that's only relevant if multiple threads call `write` on the same socket, which shouldn't happen in the default configuration.

But wait, maybe there's an issue with the `BufferedOutputStream`. The `BufferedOutputStream` is synchronized, so it's thread-safe. But what if two different threads try to write to the same response? That shouldn't happen in normal usage.

Let me think about the "content-length gets stuck" issue. If the response has a content-length header, the `BlockingOutputStream` uses non-chunked mode:

```java
if (!isChunked) {
    if (firstByte) {
        firstByte = false;
        Status usedStatus = status.get();
        sendListener.status(ctx, usedStatus);
        sendListener.headers(ctx, headers);
        BufferData growing = BufferData.growing(256 + buffer.available());
        nonEntityBytes(headers, usedStatus, growing, keepAlive, validateHeaders);
        bytesWritten += buffer.available();
        checkContentLength(buffer);
        sendListener.data(ctx, buffer);
        growing.write(buffer);
        responseBytesTotal += growing.available();
        dataWriter.write(growing);
    } else {
        writeContent(buffer);
    }
    return;
}
```

For the first write, it creates a `GrowingBufferData` and writes headers + first buffer. Then it calls `dataWriter.write(growing)`. Subsequent writes go through `writeContent(buffer)` which calls `dataWriter.write(buffer)` directly.

But wait, what if there's only one write? Then `firstByte` stays true after the write? No, `firstByte = false` is set in the first write. So subsequent writes go to the else branch.

But there's a problem: what if the first buffer is large and gets split across multiple `dataWriter.write` calls? Actually, `dataWriter.write(growing)` writes the entire growing buffer at once. The `NioSocket.write` handles splitting it into 8KB chunks internally.

For the content-length case, after all writes are done, `commit()` is called:
```java
void commit() {
    if (closed) {
        return;
    }
    this.closed = true;
    ...
    if (firstByte) {
        ...
    } else if (isChunked) {
        terminatingChunk(sendTrailers);
    }
    ...
}
```

Since `isChunked` is false (content-length was set), the `else if (isChunked)` branch is not taken. Nothing happens. This is correct because for content-length responses, no terminating chunk is needed.

But wait, what if `firstByte` is still true and `isChunked` is false? That would mean no data was written. In that case, `sendFirstChunkOnly()` is called, which sets content-length to 0. That's fine.

OK, I think I need to look at the `SmartSocketWriter` more carefully. Even though it's not the default, maybe there's a scenario where it's used. But actually, looking at the `SocketWriter.create`:

```java
public static SocketWriter create(ExecutorService executor,
                                  HelidonSocket socket,
                                  int writeQueueLength,
                                  boolean smartAsyncWrites) {
    if (writeQueueLength <= 1) {
        return new SocketWriterDirect(socket);
    } else {
        return smartAsyncWrites
                ? new SmartSocketWriter(executor, socket, writeQueueLength)
                : new SocketWriterAsync(executor, socket, writeQueueLength);
    }
}
```

With defaults (writeQueueLength=0, smartAsyncWrites=false), `writeQueueLength <= 1` is true, so `SocketWriterDirect` is used. No async writing.

But looking at the PR description again, the second reporter says:
> "After upgrading our service from Helidon 4.3.4 to 4.4.0, we started seeing rare, nondeterministic failures"

Maybe the issue is indeed something that changed in 4.4.0. Let me check the git history for recent changes to the key files.

Actually, I can't check git history since there's only one commit. Let me look at the code more carefully to find potential bugs.

Let me look at the `Http1ServerResponse.outputStream()` method:

```java
@Override
public OutputStream outputStream() {
    beforeSend();
    return outputStream(false);
}
```

And `outputStream(boolean)`:
```java
private OutputStream outputStream(boolean skipEncoders) {
    if (isSent) {
        throw new IllegalStateException("Response already sent");
    }
    if (streamingEntity) {
        throw new IllegalStateException("OutputStream already obtained");
    }
    streamingEntity = true;

    BlockingOutputStream bos = new BlockingOutputStream(...);
    int writeBufferSize = ctx.listenerContext().config().writeBufferSize();
    outputStream = new ClosingBufferedOutputStream(bos, writeBufferSize);

    OutputStream encodedOutputStream = outputStream;
    if (!skipEncoders) {
        encodedOutputStream = contentEncode(outputStream);
        bos.checkResponseHeaders();     // headers can be augmented by encoders
    }
    return outputStreamFilter == null ? encodedOutputStream : outputStreamFilter.apply(encodedOutputStream);
}
```

The `bos.checkResponseHeaders()` is called after `contentEncode()`. The `contentEncode()` method may add headers (like `Content-Encoding`). Then `checkResponseHeaders()` determines if chunked encoding should be used.

Now, look at `send(byte[], int, int)`:
```java
@Override
public void send(byte[] bytes, int position, int length) {
    if (isNoEntityStatus && length > 0) {
        status(noEntityInternalError(status()));
        return;
    }

    beforeSend();

    if (outputStreamFilter == null && !headers.contains(HeaderNames.TRAILER)) {
        byte[] entity = entityBytes(bytes, position, length);
        BufferData bufferData = (bytes != entity) ? responseBuffer(entity)
                : responseBuffer(entity, position, length);
        bytesWritten = bufferData.available();
        isSent = true;
        request.reset();
        dataWriter.write(bufferData);
        afterSend();
    } else {
        boolean skipEncoders = (length == 0);
        try (OutputStream os = outputStream(skipEncoders)) {
            os.write(bytes, position, length);
        } catch (IOException e) {
            throw new ServerConnectionException("Failed to write response", e);
        }
    }
}
```

When `outputStreamFilter != null` or trailers are present, it uses `outputStream()` and closes it. The close triggers `ClosingBufferedOutputStream.close()` which sets `closing = true` and flushes. But then `commit()` is never called! Wait, it's called later by the routing framework. Let me check...

In `HttpRoutingImpl.RoutingExecutor.call()`:
```java
if (result == RoutingResult.FINISH) {
    response.commit();
    return null;
}
```

So `commit()` is always called after the handler returns. For the `send()` path with `outputStreamFilter != null`, the handler calls `send()` which internally uses `outputStream()` and closes it. Then `commit()` is called, which calls `outputStream.commit()` → `ClosingBufferedOutputStream.commit()` → flush + `BlockingOutputStream.commit()`.

But `BlockingOutputStream.commit()` has:
```java
if (firstByte) {
    if (forcedChunked && firstBuffer != null) {
        sendHeadersAndPrepare();
        writeChunked(firstBuffer);
        terminatingChunk(sendTrailers);
    } else {
        sendFirstChunkOnly();
    }
} else if (isChunked) {
    terminatingChunk(sendTrailers);
}
```

The data has already been written to the socket via `dataWriter.write()`. But `commit()` may also write the terminating chunk for chunked responses, or may do nothing for content-length responses.

Wait, I think I found a bug! Let me look at the flow for `send()` with `outputStreamFilter != null`:

1. `send()` calls `outputStream(skipEncoders)` which creates a new `BlockingOutputStream` and `ClosingBufferedOutputStream`
2. `os.write(bytes, position, length)` writes data
3. `os.close()` → `ClosingBufferedOutputStream.close()` → `closingDelegate.closing()` + `delegate.close()`
4. `delegate.close()` → `BufferedOutputStream.close()` → flush + close
5. `BlockingOutputStream` receives the write. If it's the only write (first byte), it stores it in `firstBuffer`. 
6. Later, `commit()` is called → `ClosingBufferedOutputStream.commit()` → flush + `closingDelegate.commit()`
7. `BlockingOutputStream.commit()` → if firstByte and firstBuffer != null, it sends headers + chunked or content-length response

But wait, the data was ALREADY sent to the socket via the `BufferedOutputStream.flush()` in step 4! And then `commit()` would try to send it again via `sendHeadersAndPrepare()` + `writeChunked(firstBuffer)` or `sendFirstChunkOnly()`!

Actually no, let me re-check. In step 2, `os.write(bytes, position, length)` writes to the `ClosingBufferedOutputStream`, which writes to `BufferedOutputStream`. If the data is larger than the buffer (4096 bytes), it's written directly to `BlockingOutputStream.write()`. If smaller, it's buffered.

In step 4, `BufferedOutputStream.close()` flushes the buffer, writing any remaining data to `BlockingOutputStream`. But `BlockingOutputStream.write()` for chunked encoding stores the first write in `firstBuffer` (doesn't send it yet). So the data hasn't been sent to the socket yet!

Then in step 7, `commit()` sends the data. This is correct.

But wait, what if the data is written in multiple chunks via `BufferedOutputStream`? For example:
1. Data is 5000 bytes. `BufferedOutputStream` buffer is 4096 bytes.
2. `write(5000 bytes)` → `BufferedOutputStream.write()` sees 5000 >= 4096, flushes buffer (empty), writes directly to `BlockingOutputStream.write(5000 bytes)`
3. `BlockingOutputStream.write(5000 bytes)` → firstByte=true, firstBuffer=null → `firstBuffer = buffer.copy()` → returns without sending
4. `close()` → `BufferedOutputStream.close()` → flush (empty) → close
5. `commit()` → sends `firstBuffer` as chunked or content-length

This is correct.

But what if the data is written in multiple chunks via the application? Like:
1. User writes 2000 bytes → buffered
2. User writes 3000 bytes → buffered (total 5000 > 4096) → flush writes 4096 bytes, then buffer the remaining 904 bytes
3. The first `BlockingOutputStream.write(4096 bytes)` → firstByte=true → `firstBuffer = buffer.copy()`
4. The second `BlockingOutputStream.write(904 bytes)` → firstByte is still true! (because we returned after storing firstBuffer in step 3)
   → `if (firstByte)` is true → `sendHeadersAndPrepare()`, `BufferData combined = BufferData.create(firstBuffer, buffer)`, `writeChunked(combined)`, `firstByte = false`
5. `close()` → flush remaining → `BufferedOutputStream` is empty
6. `commit()` → firstByte=false, isChunked=true → `terminatingChunk(sendTrailers)`

This looks correct.

Hmm, but what about the case where `BufferedOutputStream` splits a write? Like:
1. User writes 10000 bytes in one call
2. `BufferedOutputStream.write(b, 0, 10000)` → 10000 >= 4096, so flush buffer (empty), then `out.write(b, 0, 10000)` directly
3. `BlockingOutputStream.write(10000 bytes)` → firstByte=true → `firstBuffer = buffer.copy()` (stores 10000 bytes)
4. `close()` → flush empty → close
5. `commit()` → sends firstBuffer

This is correct too. The `BufferedOutputStream` doesn't split the direct write.

OK, I'm running out of ideas from code inspection. Let me try to actually run a test to reproduce the issue.

Actually, let me look at one more thing. The PR description says:
> "If using chunked transfer, I occasionally see 'missing CR' or 'Malformed encoding found in chunked-encoding'"

And the second report says:
> "java.io.IOException: Chunk header size too long: 2050"

2050 is interesting. In hex, 2050 = 0x802. But what if the client is reading data bytes as chunk size? For example, if the `\r\n` after the chunk data is missing, the client would read the next chunk's size prefix as part of the data.

But wait, 2050 is also close to 2048 (0x800), which is 2^11. Could it be related to the buffer size?

Let me look at the `NioSocket.writeBuffer` size: 8192 (8KB). If a chunked encoding frame has `hex\r\n<8192 bytes>\r\n`, that's about 8200 bytes. The `writeChunked` method creates a single buffer with all of these bytes:

```java
BufferData toWrite = BufferData.create(available + hex.length + 4);
```

If `available` is, say, 524288 bytes (as in the PR example), the buffer is 524288 + 6 + 4 = 524298 bytes. This is a single `FixedBufferData` with 524298 bytes.

Then `dataWriter.write(toWrite)` → `SocketWriterDirect.write(toWrite)` → `NioSocket.write(toWrite)`.

`NioSocket.write` loops, writing 8192 bytes at a time. The first write sends `hex\r\n` + first ~8186 bytes of data. The second write sends the next 8192 bytes. Eventually the last write sends the remaining bytes + `\r\n`.

This should work correctly. The socket receives the data in 8KB chunks, but TCP is a stream protocol, so the client receives the data as a continuous stream. The chunk boundaries are preserved.

But what if there's a partial write? As I mentioned earlier, `SocketChannel.write` in blocking mode should write all bytes. But what if it doesn't? Let me verify this by looking at the JDK implementation.

Actually, I just realized something. Let me look at `NioSocket.write` more carefully:

```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
            writeBuffer.clear();
            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
            writeBuffer.flip();
            delegate.write(writeBuffer);
        }
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

The `delegate` is a `SocketChannel`. In blocking mode, `SocketChannel.write(ByteBuffer)` should write all remaining bytes in the buffer. But the JavaDoc says:

> Writes a sequence of bytes to this channel from the given buffer.
> An attempt is made to write up to r bytes to the channel, where r is the number of bytes remaining in the buffer, that is, src.remaining(), at the moment this method is invoked.

Note: "An attempt is made to write up to r bytes". This means it MAY write fewer bytes! In practice, for blocking sockets, the JDK implementation does loop until all bytes are written. But this is not guaranteed by the specification.

However, even if a partial write occurs, the outer `while (!buffer.consumed())` loop should handle it, because `buffer.consumed()` checks if all bytes have been read from the buffer. And `buffer.writeTo` advances the read position. So if a partial write happens, the next iteration will continue from where it left off.

Wait, but there's a subtle bug here! `delegate.write(writeBuffer)` writes bytes from `writeBuffer`. After the write, `writeBuffer` may still have remaining bytes (if it was a partial write). But the code doesn't check for this! It just loops back to `writeBuffer.clear()` which discards any unwritten bytes!

Let me trace through a partial write scenario:
1. `writeBuffer.clear()` → position=0, limit=8192
2. `buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available())` → writes up to 8192 bytes to writeBuffer, advances buffer's readPosition
3. `writeBuffer.flip()` → limit=8192, position=0
4. `delegate.write(writeBuffer)` → suppose it only writes 4096 bytes. `writeBuffer` now has position=4096, limit=8192
5. Loop continues because `buffer.consumed()` is false
6. `writeBuffer.clear()` → **position=0, limit=8192** → the 4096 unwritten bytes are LOST!
7. `buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available())` → writes the NEXT 8192 bytes from buffer (buffer's readPosition was already advanced in step 2)

So 4096 bytes are lost! This would corrupt the chunked encoding!

But wait, does `SocketChannel.write` in blocking mode ever return a partial write? In practice, it shouldn't for small buffers. But the JDK specification allows it. And on some OS configurations or under high load, it might happen.

However, I'm not 100% sure this is the bug because:
1. It would cause corruption much more frequently than "occasionally"
2. The PR says it started in 4.4.0, and this code has probably been there for longer

Let me verify by checking if there's a fix for this in the `NioSocket.write` method. Actually, I notice the method uses `delegate.write(writeBuffer)` without checking the return value or looping. This IS a bug, but it may not be the specific bug causing the reported issue.

Let me look at whether there's another writer implementation that handles this correctly...

Actually, I think I should focus on a different potential issue. Let me look at the `TlsNioSocket` which extends `NioSocket`:

    59	    private TlsNioSocket(SocketChannel delegate, SSLEngine sslEngine, String channelId, String serverChannelId) {
    60	        super(delegate, channelId, serverChannelId);
    61	
    62	        this.engine = sslEngine;
    63	
    64	        SSLSession dummySession = engine.getSession();
    65	        this.peerNetData = ByteBuffer.allocate(dummySession.getPacketBufferSize());
    66	        this.peerAppData = ByteBuffer.allocate(dummySession.getApplicationBufferSize());
    67	        this.myNetData = ByteBuffer.allocate(dummySession.getPacketBufferSize());
    68	        this.myAppData = ByteBuffer.allocate(dummySession.getApplicationBufferSize());
    69	        dummySession.invalidate();
    70	    }

   100	        sslEngine.setUseClientMode(true);

   104	    @Override
   105	    public PeerInfo remotePeer() {
   106	        if (renegotiated()) {
   107	            remotePeer = null;
   108	            localPeer = null;
   109	        }
   110	
   111	        if (remotePeer == null) {
   112	            this.remotePeer = PeerInfoImpl.createRemote(this);
   113	        }

   120	            remotePeer = null;
   121	            localPeer = null;
   122	        }
   123	
   124	        if (localPeer == null) {
   125	            this.localPeer = PeerInfoImpl.createLocal(this);
   126	        }

   132	        return true;

   137	        String protocol = engine.getApplicationProtocol();
   138	        return protocol != null && !protocol.isEmpty();
   139	    }

   143	        String protocol = engine.getApplicationProtocol();
   144	        if (protocol == null || protocol.isEmpty()) {
   145	            throw new NoSuchElementException("No protocol negotiated, guard with #protocolNegotiated()");
   146	        }
   147	        return protocol;
   148	    }
   149	
   150	    @Override
   151	    public byte[] get() {
   152	        try {
   153	            peerAppData.clear();
   154	
   155	            while (peerAppData.position() == 0) {
   156	                SSLEngineResult result = receiveAndUnwrap();
   157	                SSLEngineResult.Status status = result.getStatus();
   158	
   159	                if (status == SSLEngineResult.Status.CLOSED) {
   160	                    doClosure();
   161	                    return appBytes();
   162	                }
   163	
   164	                SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus handshakeStatus = result.getHandshakeStatus();
   165	                if (handshakeStatus != SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus.FINISHED
   166	                        && handshakeStatus != SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus.NOT_HANDSHAKING) {
   167	                    doHandshake(handshakeStatus);
   168	                }
   169	            }
   170	
   171	            return appBytes();
   172	        } catch (DataReader.InsufficientDataAvailableException e) {
   173	            // connection closed
   174	            return null;
   175	        } catch (IOException e) {
   176	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   177	        }
   178	    }
   179

   183	            return doRead(buffer);
   184	        } catch (IOException e) {
   185	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   186	        }
   187	    }
   188	
   189	    @Override
   190	    public void write(BufferData buffer) {
   191	        try {
   192	            doWrite(buffer);
   193	        } catch (IOException e) {
   194	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   195	        }
   196	    }
   197

   200	        try {
   201	            engine.closeOutbound();
   202	            doClosure();
   203	        } catch (IOException e) {
   204	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   205	        } finally {
   206	            super.close();
   207	        }
   208	    }

   224	    }
   225	
   226	    Optional<Principal> tlsPrincipal() {
   227	        return Optional.ofNullable(engine.getSession().getLocalPrincipal());
   228	    }
   229	
   230	    Optional<Certificate[]> tlsCertificates() {
   231	        return Optional.ofNullable(engine.getSession().getLocalCertificates());
   232	    }
   233	
   234	    void doClosure() throws IOException {
   235	        try {
   236	            handshakeLock.lock();
   237	            myAppData.clear();
   238	
   239	            SSLEngineResult.Status st;
   240	            SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus hs;
   241	            do {
   242	                myAppData.flip();
   243	                SSLEngineResult r = wrapAndSend(myAppData, true);
   244	                hs = r.getHandshakeStatus();
   245	                st = r.getStatus();
   246	            } while (st != SSLEngineResult.Status.CLOSED
   247	                    && !(st == SSLEngineResult.Status.OK && hs == SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus.NOT_HANDSHAKING));
   248	        } finally {
   249	            handshakeLock.unlock();
   250	        }
   251	    }
   252	
   253	    private SSLEngineResult receiveAndUnwrap() throws SSLException {
   254	        SSLEngineResult result;
   255	        SSLEngineResult.Status status;
   256	        if (closed) {
   257	            throw new DataReader.InsufficientDataAvailableException();
   258	        }
   259	        boolean needData;
   260	        if (unwrapRemaining > 0) {
   261	            peerNetData.compact();
   262	            peerNetData.flip();
   263	            needData = false;
   264	        } else {
   265	            peerNetData.clear();
   266	            needData = true;
   267	        }
   268	
   269	        int x;
   270	        do {
   271	            if (needData) {
   272	                do {
   273	                    x = read(peerNetData);
   274	                } while (x == 0);
   275	                if (x == -1) {
   276	                    throw new DataReader.InsufficientDataAvailableException();
   277	                }
   278	                peerNetData.flip();
   279	            }
   280	            result = engine.unwrap(peerNetData, peerAppData);
   281	            status = result.getStatus();
   282	            if (status == SSLEngineResult.Status.BUFFER_UNDERFLOW) {
   283	                if (peerNetData.limit() == peerNetData.capacity()) {
   284	                    peerNetData = reallocate(peerNetData, engine.getSession().getPacketBufferSize(), false);
   285	                } else {
   286	                    peerNetData.position(peerNetData.limit());
   287	                    peerNetData.limit(peerNetData.capacity());
   288	                }
   289	                needData = true;
   290	            } else if (status == SSLEngineResult.Status.BUFFER_OVERFLOW) {
   291	                peerAppData = reallocate(peerAppData, engine.getSession().getApplicationBufferSize(), true);
   292	                needData = false;
   293	            } else if (status == SSLEngineResult.Status.CLOSED) {
   294	                closed = true;
   295	                peerAppData.flip();
   296	                return result;
   297	            }
   298	        } while (status != SSLEngineResult.Status.OK);
   299	
   300	        unwrapRemaining = peerNetData.remaining();
   301	        return result;
   302	    }
   303	
   304	    private byte[] appBytes() {
   305	        peerAppData.flip();
   306	        byte[] result = new byte[peerAppData.remaining()];
   307	        peerAppData.get(result);
   308	        return result;
   309	    }
   310	
   311	    private void doHandshake(SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus handshakeStatus) throws IOException {
   312	
   313	        SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus status = handshakeStatus;
   314	        try {
   315	            handshakeLock.lock();
   316	            myAppData.clear();
   317	
   318	            while (status != SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus.FINISHED
   319	                    && status != SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus.NOT_HANDSHAKING) {
   320	
   321	                SSLEngineResult result = null;
   322	
   323	                switch (status) {
   324	                case NEED_TASK:
   325	                    Runnable task;
   326	                    while ((task = engine.getDelegatedTask()) != null) {
   327	                        task.run();
   328	                    }
   329	                    // fall through to wrap
   330	                case NEED_WRAP:
   331	                    myAppData.clear();
   332	                    myAppData.flip();
   333	                    result = wrapAndSend(myAppData, false);
   334	                    break;
   335	                case NEED_UNWRAP:
   336	                    peerAppData.clear();
   337	                    result = receiveAndUnwrap();
   338	                    break;
   339	                default:
   340	                    throw new IllegalStateException("Unexpected status: " + status);
   341	                }
   342	
   343	                status = result.getHandshakeStatus();
   344	            }
   345	        } finally {
   346	            handshakeLock.unlock();
   347	        }
   348	    }
   349	
   350	    private int doRead(BufferData buf) throws IOException {
   351	        peerNetData.clear();
   352	        var bytesRead = read(peerNetData);
   353	        if (bytesRead > 0) {
   354	            peerNetData.flip();
   355	            while (peerNetData.hasRemaining()) {
   356	                peerAppData.clear();
   357	                var result = engine.unwrap(peerNetData, peerAppData);
   358	                switch (result.getStatus()) {
   359	                case OK:
   360	                    peerAppData.flip();
   361	                    break;
   362	                case BUFFER_OVERFLOW:
   363	                    peerAppData = bufferOverflow(peerAppData, engine.getSession().getApplicationBufferSize());
   364	                    break;
   365	                case BUFFER_UNDERFLOW:
   366	                    peerNetData = bufferUnderflow(peerNetData, engine.getSession().getApplicationBufferSize());
   367	                    break;
   368	                case CLOSED:
   369	                    close();
   370	                    return -1;
   371	                default:
   372	                    throw new IllegalStateException("Invalid status: " + result.getStatus());
   373	                }
   374	            }
   375	
   376	        } else if (bytesRead == -1) {
   377	            engine.closeInbound();
   378	        }
   379	        return buf.readFrom(peerAppData);
   380	    }
   381	
   382	    private void doWrite(BufferData buffer) throws IOException {
   383	        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
   384	            myAppData.clear();
   385	            buffer.writeTo(myAppData, buffer.available());
   386	            myAppData.flip();
   387	
   388	            while (myAppData.hasRemaining()) {
   389	                SSLEngineResult result = wrapAndSend(myAppData, false);
   390	                SSLEngineResult.Status status = result.getStatus();
   391	                if (status == SSLEngineResult.Status.CLOSED) {
   392	                    doClosure();
   393	                    return;
   394	                }
   395	                SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus handshakeStatus = result.getHandshakeStatus();
   396	                if (handshakeStatus != SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus.FINISHED
   397	                        && handshakeStatus != SSLEngineResult.HandshakeStatus.NOT_HANDSHAKING) {
   398	                    doHandshake(handshakeStatus);
   399	                }
   400	            }
   401	        }
   402	    }
   403	
   404	    private SSLEngineResult wrapAndSend(ByteBuffer appData, boolean ignoreClose) throws SSLException {
   405	        if (closed && !ignoreClose) {
   406	            throw new SSLException("Engine is closed");
   407	        }
   408	        SSLEngineResult.Status status;
   409	        SSLEngineResult result;
   410	
   411	        myNetData.clear();
   412	        do {
   413	            result = engine.wrap(appData, myNetData);
   414	            status = result.getStatus();
   415	            if (status == SSLEngineResult.Status.BUFFER_OVERFLOW) {
   416	                this.myNetData = reallocate(myNetData,
   417	                                            engine.getSession().getPacketBufferSize(),
   418	                                            true);
   419	            }
   420	        } while (status == SSLEngineResult.Status.BUFFER_OVERFLOW);
   421	
   422	        if (status == SSLEngineResult.Status.CLOSED && !ignoreClose) {
   423	            closed = true;
   424	        }
   425	
   426	        if (result.bytesProduced() > 0) {
   427	            myNetData.flip();
   428	            int len = myNetData.remaining();
   429	            while (len > 0) {
   430	                len -= write(myNetData);
   431	            }
   432	        }
   433	
   434	        return result;
   435	    }
   436	
   437	    private ByteBuffer reallocate(ByteBuffer buffer, int size, boolean flip) {
   438	        if (size <= buffer.capacity()) {
   439	            size++;
   440	        }
   441	        ByteBuffer newBuffer = ByteBuffer.allocate(size);
   442	        if (flip) {
   443	            buffer.flip();
   444	        }
   445	        newBuffer.put(buffer);
   446	        return newBuffer;
   447	    }
   448	
   449	    private ByteBuffer bufferOverflow(ByteBuffer buf, int proposedCapacity) {
   450	        if (proposedCapacity > buf.capacity()) {
   451	            return ByteBuffer.allocate(proposedCapacity);
   452	        }
   453	        return buf.compact();
   454	    }
   455	
   456	    private ByteBuffer bufferUnderflow(ByteBuffer buf, int proposedCapacity) {
   457	        if (proposedCapacity <= buf.capacity()) {
   458	            return buf;
   459	        }
   460	        return ByteBuffer.allocate(proposedCapacity).put(buf.flip());
   461	    }
   462	
   463	    /**
   464	     * Check if TLS renegotiation happened,
   465	     * if so ssl session id would have changed.
   466	     *
   467	     * @return true if tls was renegotiated
   468	     */
   469	    boolean renegotiated() {
   470	        byte[] currentSessionId = engine.getSession().getId();
   471	
   472	        // Intentionally avoiding locking and MessageDigest.isEqual
   473	        if (Arrays.equals(currentSessionId, lastSslSessionId)) {
   474	            return false;
   475	        }
   476	
   477	        lastSslSessionId = currentSessionId;
   478	        return true;
   479	    }
   480	}

Now I see something interesting! Look at `TlsNioSocket.doWrite`:

```java
private void doWrite(BufferData buffer) throws IOException {
    while (!buffer.consumed()) {
        myAppData.clear();
        buffer.writeTo(myAppData, buffer.available());
        myAppData.flip();

        while (myAppData.hasRemaining()) {
            SSLEngineResult result = wrapAndSend(myAppData, false);
            ...
        }
    }
}
```

And `wrapAndSend`:
```java
private SSLEngineResult wrapAndSend(ByteBuffer appData, boolean ignoreClose) throws SSLException {
    ...
    myNetData.clear();
    do {
        result = engine.wrap(appData, myNetData);
        status = result.getStatus();
        if (status == SSLEngineResult.Status.BUFFER_OVERFLOW) {
            this.myNetData = reallocate(myNetData, engine.getSession().getPacketBufferSize(), true);
        }
    } while (status == SSLEngineResult.Status.BUFFER_OVERFLOW);
    
    ...
    if (result.bytesProduced() > 0) {
        myNetData.flip();
        int len = myNetData.remaining();
        while (len > 0) {
            len -= write(myNetData);  // calls super.write(ByteBuffer) which does SocketChannel.write
        }
    }
    return result;
}
```

This handles partial writes correctly! It loops `while (len > 0)` subtracting the written bytes.

But `NioSocket.write` (the base class, used for non-TLS) does NOT handle partial writes:

```java
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
            writeBuffer.clear();
            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
            writeBuffer.flip();
            delegate.write(writeBuffer);
        }
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

It just calls `delegate.write(writeBuffer)` once and assumes all bytes are written!

BUT, `SocketChannel.write` in blocking mode typically writes all bytes. The JDK implementation loops internally. Let me verify...

Actually, looking at OpenJDK source, `SocketChannelImpl.write` does NOT loop for blocking sockets! It calls `IOUtil.write` which calls `writeFromNativeBuffer` which does a single `write` syscall. The syscall may write fewer bytes than requested.

Wait, let me check again. Looking at the JDK source code:

```java
// SocketChannelImpl.java
@Override
public int write(ByteBuffer buf) throws IOException {
    ...
    try {
        ...
        do {
            n = IOUtil.write(fd, buf, -1, nd);
        } while ((n == IOStatus.INTERRUPTED) && isOpen());
        return IOStatus.normalize(n);
    } ...
}
```

This does NOT loop until all bytes are written! It only loops if interrupted. So `SocketChannel.write` can return a short write, and the code doesn't handle it.

But wait, this is for JDK 25. Let me check the actual code more carefully. The key method is `IOUtil.write`:

```java
static int write(FileDescriptor fd, ByteBuffer src, long position,
                 NativeDispatcher nd) throws IOException {
    ...
    return writeFromNativeBuffer(fd, src, position, nd);
}
```

Which does a single native write. So yes, `SocketChannel.write` in blocking mode can return fewer bytes than requested.

This is a real bug in `NioSocket.write`! If a partial write occurs, data is lost. And this would affect both chunked and content-length responses.

But why would this only start happening in 4.4.0? Maybe the NIO socket was introduced in 4.4.0? Let me check the file headers.

`NioSocket.java`: Copyright 2025 → this IS new in 4.4.0!
`TlsNioSocket.java`: Copyright 2025 → also new!

And the `PlainSocket` (old implementation) probably handles this correctly. Let me check:

2026-05-30 02:25:02,079 - INFO - swea-agent-helidon-io__helidon-11386 - 💭 THOUGHT
Now we can see the key difference!

`PlainSocket.write`:
```java
@Override
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    buffer.writeTo(outputStream);
}
```

This uses `OutputStream.write` which handles partial writes internally (the `OutputStream` contract guarantees all bytes are written). The `BufferData.writeTo(OutputStream)` method:

```java
// FixedBufferData
@Override
public void writeTo(OutputStream out) {
    try {
        out.write(bytes, readPosition, writePosition);
        readPosition = writePosition;
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

This calls `OutputStream.write(byte[], int, int)` which writes all bytes.

But `NioSocket.write`:
```java
@Override
public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        while (!buffer.consumed()) {
            writeBuffer.clear();
            buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
            writeBuffer.flip();
            delegate.write(writeBuffer);
        }
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

This uses `SocketChannel.write(ByteBuffer)` which may NOT write all bytes in a single call. The code assumes it does, which is incorrect!

And in `ConnectionHandler`, the default is `useNio = true`:
```java
@Option.DefaultBoolean(true)
boolean useNio();
```

So by default, the NIO socket is used! And the NIO socket has this bug!

This explains why the issue appeared in 4.4.0 - the NIO socket was introduced (copyright 2025) and it has a bug that the old `PlainSocket` didn't have.

Now let me also check the `TlsNioSocket` write method - it properly handles partial writes in `wrapAndSend`:
```java
if (result.bytesProduced() > 0) {
    myNetData.flip();
    int len = myNetData.remaining();
    while (len > 0) {
        len -= write(myNetData);
    }
}
```

So TLS connections are fine. But plaintext connections using `NioSocket` are broken.

Now let me fix the `NioSocket.write` method to handle partial writes:</think>Now I've found the bug! The `NioSocket.write` method doesn't handle partial writes from `SocketChannel.write`. Let me fix it:

    34	    private static final int BUFFER_LENGTH = 8 * 1024;
    35

    37	    private final ByteBuffer writeBuffer = ByteBuffer.allocate(BUFFER_LENGTH);
    38

    45	     *
    46	     * @param delegate      delegate socket
    47	     * @param childSocketId channel id
    48	     * @param socketId      server channel id
    49	     */
    50	    protected NioSocket(SocketChannel delegate, String childSocketId, String socketId) {
    51	        this.delegate = delegate;
    52	        this.childSocketId = childSocketId;
    53	        this.socketId = socketId;
    54	    }

    62	     * @return a new plain socket
    63	     */
    64	    public static NioSocket server(SocketChannel delegate, String channelId, String serverChannelId) {
    65	        return new NioSocket(delegate, channelId, serverChannelId);
    66	    }

    76	        return new NioSocket(delegate, channelId, "client");

    82	    }

    91	        return false;

   105	    public void close() {
   106	        try {
   107	            // if close() is called without shutdownOutput(), the remote sometimes does not receive last bytes sent
   108	            delegate.shutdownOutput();
   109	            delegate.shutdownInput();
   110	            delegate.close();
   111	        } catch (IOException e) {
   112	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   113	        }
   114	    }

   118	    }

   122	        return delegate.isOpen();
   123	    }

   132	                readBuffer.flip();
   133	            }
   134	            return buffer.readFrom(readBuffer);
   135	        } catch (IOException e) {

    94	    @Override
    95	    public String socketId() {
    96	        return socketId;
    97	    }
    98	
    99	    @Override
   100	    public String childSocketId() {
   101	        return childSocketId;
   102	    }
   103	
   104	    @Override
   105	    public void close() {
   106	        try {
   107	            // if close() is called without shutdownOutput(), the remote sometimes does not receive last bytes sent
   108	            delegate.shutdownOutput();
   109	            delegate.shutdownInput();
   110	            delegate.close();
   111	        } catch (IOException e) {
   112	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   113	        }
   114	    }
   115	
   116	    @Override
   117	    public void idle() {
   118	    }
   119	
   120	    @Override
   121	    public boolean isConnected() {
   122	        return delegate.isOpen();
   123	    }
   124	
   125	    @SuppressWarnings("removal")
   126	    @Override
   127	    public int read(BufferData buffer) {
   128	        try {
   129	            if (readBuffer.remaining() == 0) {
   130	                readBuffer.clear();
   131	                delegate.read(readBuffer);
   132	                readBuffer.flip();
   133	            }
   134	            return buffer.readFrom(readBuffer);
   135	        } catch (IOException e) {
   136	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   137	        }
   138	    }
   139	
   140	    @Override
   141	    public void write(BufferData buffer) {
   142	        try {
   143	            while (!buffer.consumed()) {
   144	                writeBuffer.clear();
   145	                buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
   146	                writeBuffer.flip();
   147	                delegate.write(writeBuffer);
   148	            }
   149	        } catch (IOException e) {
   150	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   151	        }
   152	    }
   153	
   154	    @Override
   155	    public byte[] get() {
   156	        try {
   157	            int r = delegate.read(readBuffer);
   158	            readBuffer.flip();
   159	            if (r == -1) {
   160	                return null; // end of data
   161	            }
   162	            if (r == 0) {
   163	                throw new IllegalStateException("Read 0 bytes, this should never happen with blocking socket");
   164	            }
   165	            byte[] result = new byte[r];
   166	            readBuffer.get(result);
   167	            return result;
   168	        } catch (IOException e) {
   169	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   170	        } finally {
   171	            readBuffer.clear();
   172	        }
   173	    }
   174	
   175	    /**
   176	     * Write to the underlying socket/channel from the provided buffer.
   177	     * The buffer is not flipped.
   178	     *
   179	     * @param buffer buffer to write
   180	     * @return number of bytes written
   181	     */
   182	    protected int write(ByteBuffer buffer) {
   183	        try {
   184	            return delegate.write(buffer);
   185	        } catch (IOException e) {
   186	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   187	        }
   188	    }
   189	
   190	    /**
   191	     * Read from the underlying socket/channel into the provided buffer.
   192	     * The buffer is not flipped.
   193	     *
   194	     * @param buffer buffer to read to
   195	     * @return number of bytes read
   196	     */
   197	    protected int read(ByteBuffer buffer) {
   198	        try {
   199	            return delegate.read(buffer);
   200	        } catch (IOException e) {
   201	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   202	        }
   203	    }
   204	
   205	    SocketAddress localSocketAddress() {
   206	        try {
   207	            return delegate.getLocalAddress();
   208	        } catch (IOException e) {
   209	            return null;
   210	        }
   211	    }
   212	
   213	    SocketAddress remoteSocketAddress() {
   214	        try {
   215	            return delegate.getRemoteAddress();
   216	        } catch (IOException e) {
   217	            return null;
   218	        }
   219	    }
   220	
   221	    String localHost() {
   222	        SocketAddress localSocketAddress = localSocketAddress();
   223	        if (localSocketAddress instanceof InetSocketAddress inet) {
   224	            return inet.getHostString();
   225	        }
   226	        if (localSocketAddress instanceof UnixDomainSocketAddress unix) {
   227	            return unix.getPath().toString();
   228	        }
   229	        throw new IllegalStateException("Local host is not a supported socket address. Address: "
   230	                                                + localSocketAddress.getClass().getName());
   231	    }
   232	
   233	    String remoteHost() {
   234	        SocketAddress remoteSocketAddress = remoteSocketAddress();
   235	        if (remoteSocketAddress instanceof InetSocketAddress inet) {
   236	            return inet.getHostString();
   237	        }
   238	        if (remoteSocketAddress instanceof UnixDomainSocketAddress unix) {
   239	            return unix.getPath().toString();
   240	        }
   241	        throw new IllegalStateException("Remote host is not a supported socket address. Address: "
   242	                                                + remoteSocketAddress.getClass().getName());
   243	    }
   244	
   245	    int localPort() {
   246	        SocketAddress localSocketAddress = localSocketAddress();
   247	        if (localSocketAddress instanceof InetSocketAddress inet) {
   248	            return inet.getPort();
   249	        }
   250	        if (localSocketAddress instanceof UnixDomainSocketAddress) {
   251	            return -1;
   252	        }
   253	        throw new IllegalStateException("Local host is not an a supported socket address. Address: "
   254	                                                + localSocketAddress.getClass().getName());
   255	    }
   256	
   257	    int remotePort() {
   258	        SocketAddress remoteSocketAddress = remoteSocketAddress();
   259	        if (remoteSocketAddress instanceof InetSocketAddress inet) {
   260	            return inet.getPort();
   261	        }
   262	        if (remoteSocketAddress instanceof UnixDomainSocketAddress) {
   263	            return -1;
   264	        }
   265	        throw new IllegalStateException("Remote host is not an a supported socket address. Address: "
   266	                                                + remoteSocketAddress.getClass().getName());
   267	    }
   268	}

                writeBuffer.clear();
                buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());

                while (writeBuffer.hasRemaining()) {

                }

The fix has been applied. Now let me also check if there's a similar issue in the `read` method. The `read` method at line 127-138:

```java
public int read(BufferData buffer) {
    try {
        if (readBuffer.remaining() == 0) {
            readBuffer.clear();
            delegate.read(readBuffer);
            readBuffer.flip();
        }
        return buffer.readFrom(readBuffer);
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

The `read` method uses `delegate.read(readBuffer)` which may return 0 or a short read. But this is in a method that returns `int` (number of bytes read). The caller is expected to handle short reads. Let me check how this is called.

Looking at `DataReader` and related classes, the `HelidonSocket.read(BufferData)` is called by the `DataReader` which should handle partial reads correctly. So this might be fine.

But actually, `delegate.read(readBuffer)` in blocking mode should block until at least 1 byte is read. And since `readBuffer` is 8192 bytes, it should fill up with available data. If it returns fewer bytes, that's fine - the caller will just get fewer bytes.

The important thing is that the `write` method now properly handles partial writes by looping until all bytes in the `writeBuffer` are written.

Now let me also check the `SmartSocketWriter` race condition issue. While it's not the default, it's still a potential bug. Let me look at it again:

The issue: when switching from async to sync mode, both the async writer thread and the main thread could write concurrently.

Let me fix the `SmartSocketWriter` to properly synchronize the transition:

    17	package io.helidon.common.socket;
    18	
    19	import java.util.concurrent.ExecutorService;
    20	
    21	import io.helidon.common.buffers.BufferData;
    22	
    23	/**
    24	 * A special socket write that starts async but may switch to sync mode if it
    25	 * detects that the async queue size is below {@link #QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD}.
    26	 * If it switches to sync mode, it shall never return back to async mode.
    27	 */
    28	public class SmartSocketWriter extends SocketWriter {
    29	    private static final long WINDOW_SIZE = 1000;
    30	    private static final double QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD = 2.0;
    31	
    32	    private final SocketWriterAsync asyncWriter;
    33	    private volatile long windowIndex;
    34	    private volatile boolean asyncMode;
    35	
    36	    SmartSocketWriter(ExecutorService executor, HelidonSocket socket, int writeQueueLength) {
    37	        super(socket);
    38	        this.asyncWriter = new SocketWriterAsync(executor, socket, writeQueueLength);
    39	        this.asyncMode = true;
    40	        this.windowIndex = 0L;
    41	    }
    42	
    43	    @Override
    44	    public void write(BufferData... buffers) {
    45	        for (BufferData buffer : buffers) {
    46	            write(buffer);
    47	        }
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    @Override
    51	    public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    52	        if (asyncMode) {
    53	            asyncWriter.write(buffer);
    54	            if (++windowIndex % WINDOW_SIZE == 0 && asyncWriter.avgQueueSize() < QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD) {
    55	                asyncMode = false;
    56	            }
    57	        } else {
    58	            asyncWriter.drainQueue();
    59	            writeNow(buffer);       // blocking write
    60	        }
    61	    }
    62	}

    17	package io.helidon.common.socket;
    18	
    19	import java.util.concurrent.ExecutorService;
    20	
    21	import io.helidon.common.buffers.BufferData;
    22	
    23	/**
    24	 * A special socket write that starts async but may switch to sync mode if it
    25	 * detects that the async queue size is below {@link #QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD}.
    26	 * If it switches to sync mode, it shall never return back to async mode.
    27	 */
    28	public class SmartSocketWriter extends SocketWriter {
    29	    private static final long WINDOW_SIZE = 1000;
    30	    private static final double QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD = 2.0;
    31	
    32	    private final SocketWriterAsync asyncWriter;
    33	    private volatile long windowIndex;
    34	    private volatile boolean asyncMode;
    35	
    36	    SmartSocketWriter(ExecutorService executor, HelidonSocket socket, int writeQueueLength) {
    37	        super(socket);
    38	        this.asyncWriter = new SocketWriterAsync(executor, socket, writeQueueLength);
    39	        this.asyncMode = true;
    40	        this.windowIndex = 0L;
    41	    }
    42	
    43	    @Override
    44	    public void write(BufferData... buffers) {
    45	        for (BufferData buffer : buffers) {
    46	            write(buffer);
    47	        }
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    @Override
    51	    @Override
    52	    public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    53	        if (asyncMode) {
    54	            asyncWriter.write(buffer);
    55	            if (++windowIndex % WINDOW_SIZE == 0 && asyncWriter.avgQueueSize() < QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD) {
    56	                asyncMode = false;
    57	                asyncWriter.drainQueue();
    58	            }
    59	        } else {
    60	            writeNow(buffer);       // blocking write
    61	        }
    62	    }
    63	}

    17	package io.helidon.common.socket;
    18	
    19	import java.util.concurrent.ExecutorService;
    20	
    21	import io.helidon.common.buffers.BufferData;
    22	
    23	/**
    24	 * A special socket write that starts async but may switch to sync mode if it
    25	 * detects that the async queue size is below {@link #QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD}.
    26	 * If it switches to sync mode, it shall never return back to async mode.
    27	 */
    28	public class SmartSocketWriter extends SocketWriter {
    29	    private static final long WINDOW_SIZE = 1000;
    30	    private static final double QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD = 2.0;
    31	
    32	    private final SocketWriterAsync asyncWriter;
    33	    private volatile long windowIndex;
    34	    private volatile boolean asyncMode;
    35	
    36	    SmartSocketWriter(ExecutorService executor, HelidonSocket socket, int writeQueueLength) {
    37	        super(socket);
    38	        this.asyncWriter = new SocketWriterAsync(executor, socket, writeQueueLength);
    39	        this.asyncMode = true;
    40	        this.windowIndex = 0L;
    41	    }
    42	
    43	    @Override
    44	    public void write(BufferData... buffers) {
    45	        for (BufferData buffer : buffers) {
    46	            write(buffer);
    47	        }
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    @Override
    51	    public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    52	        if (asyncMode) {
    53	            asyncWriter.write(buffer);
    54	            if (++windowIndex % WINDOW_SIZE == 0 && asyncWriter.avgQueueSize() < QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD) {
    55	                asyncMode = false;
    56	                asyncWriter.drainQueue();
    57	            }
    58	            asyncWriter.drainQueue();
    59	            writeNow(buffer);       // blocking write
    60	        }
    61	    }
    62	}

    20	
    21	import io.helidon.common.buffers.BufferData;
    22	
    23	/**
    24	 * A special socket write that starts async but may switch to sync mode if it
    25	 * detects that the async queue size is below {@link #QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD}.
    26	 * If it switches to sync mode, it shall never return back to async mode.
    27	 */
    28	public class SmartSocketWriter extends SocketWriter {
    29	    private static final long WINDOW_SIZE = 1000;
    30	    private static final double QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD = 2.0;
    31	
    32	    private final SocketWriterAsync asyncWriter;
    33	    private volatile long windowIndex;
    34	    private volatile boolean asyncMode;
    35	
    36	    SmartSocketWriter(ExecutorService executor, HelidonSocket socket, int writeQueueLength) {
    37	        super(socket);
    38	        this.asyncWriter = new SocketWriterAsync(executor, socket, writeQueueLength);
    39	        this.asyncMode = true;
    40	        this.windowIndex = 0L;
    41	    }
    42	
    43	    @Override
    44	    public void write(BufferData... buffers) {
    45	        for (BufferData buffer : buffers) {
    46	            write(buffer);
    47	        }
    48	    }
    49	
    50	    @Override
    51	    public void write(BufferData buffer) {
    52	        if (asyncMode) {
    53	            asyncWriter.write(buffer);
    54	            if (++windowIndex % WINDOW_SIZE == 0 && asyncWriter.avgQueueSize() < QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD) {
    55	                asyncMode = false;
    56	            }
    57	        } else {
    58	            asyncWriter.drainQueue();
    59	            writeNow(buffer);       // blocking write
    60	        }
    61	    }
    62	}

package io.helidon.common.socket;

import java.util.concurrent.ExecutorService;

import io.helidon.common.buffers.BufferData;

/**
 * A special socket write that starts async but may switch to sync mode if it
 * detects that the async queue size is below {@link #QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD}.
 * If it switches to sync mode, it shall never return back to async mode.
 */
public class SmartSocketWriter extends SocketWriter {
    private static final long WINDOW_SIZE = 1000;
    private static final double QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD = 2.0;

    private final SocketWriterAsync asyncWriter;
    private volatile long windowIndex;
    private volatile boolean asyncMode;

    SmartSocketWriter(ExecutorService executor, HelidonSocket socket, int writeQueueLength) {
        super(socket);
        this.asyncWriter = new SocketWriterAsync(executor, socket, writeQueueLength);
        this.asyncMode = true;
        this.windowIndex = 0L;
    }

    @Override
    public void write(BufferData... buffers) {
        for (BufferData buffer : buffers) {
            write(buffer);
        }
    }

    @Override
    public void write(BufferData buffer) {
        if (asyncMode) {
            asyncWriter.write(buffer);
            if (++windowIndex % WINDOW_SIZE == 0 && asyncWriter.avgQueueSize() < QUEUE_SIZE_THRESHOLD) {
                asyncMode = false;
                asyncWriter.drainQueue();
            }
        } else {
            writeNow(buffer);       // blocking write
        }
    }
}

    35

    41	    }

    17	package io.helidon.common.socket;
    18	
    19	import java.io.IOException;
    20	import java.io.UncheckedIOException;
    21	import java.net.InetSocketAddress;
    22	import java.net.SocketAddress;
    23	import java.net.UnixDomainSocketAddress;
    24	import java.nio.ByteBuffer;
    25	import java.nio.channels.SocketChannel;
    26	
    27	import io.helidon.common.buffers.BufferData;
    28	
    29	/**
    30	 * Plain socket based on NIO {@link java.nio.channels.SocketChannel}.
    31	 * This socket uses ByteBuffer for reading and writing.
    32	 */
    33	public sealed class NioSocket implements HelidonSocket permits TlsNioSocket {
    34	    private static final int BUFFER_LENGTH = 8 * 1024;
    35	
    36	    private final ByteBuffer readBuffer = ByteBuffer.allocate(BUFFER_LENGTH);
    37	    private final ByteBuffer writeBuffer = ByteBuffer.allocate(BUFFER_LENGTH);
    38	
    39	    private final SocketChannel delegate;
    40	    private final String childSocketId;
    41	    private final String socketId;
    42	
    43	    /**
    44	     * Plain socket.
    45	     *
    46	     * @param delegate      delegate socket
    47	     * @param childSocketId channel id
    48	     * @param socketId      server channel id
    49	     */
    50	    protected NioSocket(SocketChannel delegate, String childSocketId, String socketId) {
    51	        this.delegate = delegate;
    52	        this.childSocketId = childSocketId;
    53	        this.socketId = socketId;
    54	    }
    55	
    56	    /**
    57	     * Create a new server socket.
    58	     *
    59	     * @param delegate        underlying socket
    60	     * @param channelId       channel id
    61	     * @param serverChannelId server channel id
    62	     * @return a new plain socket
    63	     */
    64	    public static NioSocket server(SocketChannel delegate, String channelId, String serverChannelId) {
    65	        return new NioSocket(delegate, channelId, serverChannelId);
    66	    }
    67	
    68	    /**
    69	     * Create a new client socket.
    70	     *
    71	     * @param delegate  underlying socket
    72	     * @param channelId channel id
    73	     * @return a new plain socket
    74	     */
    75	    public static NioSocket client(SocketChannel delegate, String channelId) {
    76	        return new NioSocket(delegate, channelId, "client");
    77	    }
    78	
    79	    @Override
    80	    public PeerInfo remotePeer() {
    81	        return PeerInfoImpl.createRemote(this);
    82	    }
    83	
    84	    @Override
    85	    public PeerInfo localPeer() {
    86	        return PeerInfoImpl.createLocal(this);
    87	    }
    88	
    89	    @Override
    90	    public boolean isSecure() {
    91	        return false;
    92	    }
    93	
    94	    @Override
    95	    public String socketId() {
    96	        return socketId;
    97	    }
    98	
    99	    @Override
   100	    public String childSocketId() {
   101	        return childSocketId;
   102	    }
   103	
   104	    @Override
   105	    public void close() {
   106	        try {
   107	            // if close() is called without shutdownOutput(), the remote sometimes does not receive last bytes sent
   108	            delegate.shutdownOutput();
   109	            delegate.shutdownInput();
   110	            delegate.close();
   111	        } catch (IOException e) {
   112	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   113	        }
   114	    }
   115	
   116	    @Override
   117	    public void idle() {
   118	    }
   119	
   120	    @Override
   121	    public boolean isConnected() {
   122	        return delegate.isOpen();
   123	    }
   124	
   125	    @SuppressWarnings("removal")
   126	    @Override
   127	    public int read(BufferData buffer) {
   128	        try {
   129	            if (readBuffer.remaining() == 0) {
   130	                readBuffer.clear();
   131	                delegate.read(readBuffer);
   132	                readBuffer.flip();
   133	            }
   134	            return buffer.readFrom(readBuffer);
   135	        } catch (IOException e) {
   136	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   137	        }
   138	    }
   139	
   140	    @Override
   141	    public void write(BufferData buffer) {
   142	        try {
   143	            while (!buffer.consumed()) {
   144	                writeBuffer.clear();
   145	                buffer.writeTo(writeBuffer, buffer.available());
   146	                writeBuffer.flip();
   147	                while (writeBuffer.hasRemaining()) {
   148	                    delegate.write(writeBuffer);
   149	                }
   150	            }
   151	        } catch (IOException e) {
   152	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   153	        }
   154	    }
   155	
   156	    @Override
   157	    public byte[] get() {
   158	        try {
   159	            int r = delegate.read(readBuffer);
   160	            readBuffer.flip();
   161	            if (r == -1) {
   162	                return null; // end of data
   163	            }
   164	            if (r == 0) {
   165	                throw new IllegalStateException("Read 0 bytes, this should never happen with blocking socket");
   166	            }
   167	            byte[] result = new byte[r];
   168	            readBuffer.get(result);
   169	            return result;
   170	        } catch (IOException e) {
   171	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   172	        } finally {
   173	            readBuffer.clear();
   174	        }
   175	    }
   176	
   177	    /**
   178	     * Write to the underlying socket/channel from the provided buffer.
   179	     * The buffer is not flipped.
   180	     *
   181	     * @param buffer buffer to write
   182	     * @return number of bytes written
   183	     */
   184	    protected int write(ByteBuffer buffer) {
   185	        try {
   186	            return delegate.write(buffer);
   187	        } catch (IOException e) {
   188	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   189	        }
   190	    }
   191	
   192	    /**
   193	     * Read from the underlying socket/channel into the provided buffer.
   194	     * The buffer is not flipped.
   195	     *
   196	     * @param buffer buffer to read to
   197	     * @return number of bytes read
   198	     */
   199	    protected int read(ByteBuffer buffer) {
   200	        try {
   201	            return delegate.read(buffer);
   202	        } catch (IOException e) {
   203	            throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
   204	        }
   205	    }
   206	
   207	    SocketAddress localSocketAddress() {
   208	        try {
   209	            return delegate.getLocalAddress();
   210	        } catch (IOException e) {
   211	            return null;
   212	        }
   213	    }
   214	
   215	    SocketAddress remoteSocketAddress() {
   216	        try {
   217	            return delegate.getRemoteAddress();
   218	        } catch (IOException e) {
   219	            return null;
   220	        }
   221	    }
   222	
   223	    String localHost() {
   224	        SocketAddress localSocketAddress = localSocketAddress();
   225	        if (localSocketAddress instanceof InetSocketAddress inet) {
   226	            return inet.getHostString();
   227	        }
   228	        if (localSocketAddress instanceof UnixDomainSocketAddress unix) {
   229	            return unix.getPath().toString();
   230	        }
   231	        throw new IllegalStateException("Local host is not a supported socket address. Address: "
   232	                                                + localSocketAddress.getClass().getName());
   233	    }
   234	
   235	    String remoteHost() {
   236	        SocketAddress remoteSocketAddress = remoteSocketAddress();
   237	        if (remoteSocketAddress instanceof InetSocketAddress inet) {
   238	            return inet.getHostString();
   239	        }
   240	        if (remoteSocketAddress instanceof UnixDomainSocketAddress unix) {
   241	            return unix.getPath().toString();
   242	        }
   243	        throw new IllegalStateException("Remote host is not a supported socket address. Address: "
   244	                                                + remoteSocketAddress.getClass().getName());
   245	    }
   246	
   247	    int localPort() {
   248	        SocketAddress localSocketAddress = localSocketAddress();
   249	        if (localSocketAddress instanceof InetSocketAddress inet) {
   250	            return inet.getPort();
   251	        }
   252	        if (localSocketAddress instanceof UnixDomainSocketAddress) {
   253	            return -1;
   254	        }
   255	        throw new IllegalStateException("Local host is not an a supported socket address. Address: "
   256	                                                + localSocketAddress.getClass().getName());
   257	    }
   258	
   259	    int remotePort() {
   260	        SocketAddress remoteSocketAddress = remoteSocketAddress();
   261	        if (remoteSocketAddress instanceof InetSocketAddress inet) {
   262	            return inet.getPort();
   263	        }
   264	        if (remoteSocketAddress instanceof UnixDomainSocketAddress) {
   265	            return -1;
   266	        }
   267	        throw new IllegalStateException("Remote host is not an a supported socket address. Address: "
   268	                                                + remoteSocketAddress.getClass().getName());
   269	    }
   270	}

Both fixes are applied. Now let me also check if there's an issue with the `PlainSocket` write method using `BufferData.writeTo(OutputStream)`. Let me verify it handles partial writes:

```java
// FixedBufferData.writeTo(OutputStream)
public void writeTo(OutputStream out) {
    try {
        out.write(bytes, readPosition, writePosition);
        readPosition = writePosition;
    } catch (IOException e) {
        throw new UncheckedIOException(e);
    }
}
```

This calls `OutputStream.write(byte[], int, int)` which contracts to write all bytes. So this is safe.

Now let me think about edge cases and verify my fixes are complete.

The main fix is in `NioSocket.write()` - adding a loop to handle partial writes from `SocketChannel.write()`. This explains:
1. "missing CR" / "Malformed encoding found in chunked-encoding" - partial writes would corrupt the chunked encoding format
2. "transfer occasionally just gets stuck completely" - if the socket write returns 0 bytes written (which can happen), the outer while loop would spin forever

The `SmartSocketWriter` fix addresses a race condition that could cause concurrent writes to the same socket, which would also corrupt data.

   354	
   355	        @Override
   356	        public void write(BufferData buffer) {
   357	            // no buffering, just write now
   358	            if (writerBuffer == null) {
   359	                writeNow(buffer);
   360	                return;
   361	            }
   362	            // have space in writerBuffer?
   363	            if (buffer.available() <= writerBuffer.capacity()) {
   364	                writerBuffer.write(buffer);
   365	                return;
   366	            }
   367	            // write and reset writerBuffer if we have data
   368	            if (writerBuffer.available() > 0) {
   369	                writeNow(writerBuffer);
   370	                writerBuffer.reset();
   371	                // have space now?
   372	                if (buffer.available() <= writerBuffer.capacity()) {
   373	                    writerBuffer.write(buffer);
   374	                    return;
   375	                }
   376	            }
   377	            // no luck, we need to write it now
   378	            writeNow(buffer);
   379	        }
   380

   382	        public void writeNow(BufferData... buffers) {
   383	            flush();

   385	                helidonSocket.write(buffer);
   386	            }
